Wang Keming Arrives in Tianjin from Beiping Yesterday; Talks with Song Resulted in a Satisfactory Outcome; North China to Form a Separate Economic Organization 18

(Tianjin) Wang Keming, Wang Yitang, and Cao Rulin arrived in Tianjin from Beiping by train at noon on the 12th. Zhang Zizhong and the heads of various municipal bureaus welcomed them at the station. It is scheduled to visit Zhang Zhongchang's residence at 10:00 AM on the 13th and then visit Tashiro to discuss economic cooperation issues. He will return south on the 14th. According to him, although there were discussions with Song Zheyuan in Beiping regarding economic development in North China, there were no concrete results. His visit to Tashiro is still to exchange opinions. After returning south, he will come north again at the end of the month. As he is old and weak, he still needs to consider whether or not to accept the position of chairman of the Economic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council before making a decision. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

(Beiping) Wang Keming arrived in Beiping from Tianjin on the 9th and repeatedly met with Song and Shimizu, a counselor at the Japanese Embassy, to exchange views on Sino-Japanese economic cooperation issues in North China. After staying in Beiping for three days, the results of contacts with various parties were satisfactory. He left Beiping for Tianjin this morning, accompanied by Wang Yitang and Cao Rulin. Wang said that the results of the talks with Song were satisfactory. He will go to Tianjin for further talks and, if time permits, plans to return to Beiping tonight; otherwise, he will leave Tianjin on the 13th. After contacting the people in Beiping, he will return north at the end of this month. Song repeatedly asked him to stay in Beiping to help. He will consider this matter the next time he is in Beiping. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

(Beiping) Prior to his departure, Wang Keming, who went to Tianjin this morning to visit Tashiro and then went south to enter Beijing, told a guest that he might return to Beiping in a few days. When asked whether he would assume the position of chairman of the Economic Committee of the Hebei-Chahar Political Council, Wang replied that Song Zheyuan did intend to entrust him with this task, but it had not yet been decided. (Reuters dispatch from the 12th)

(Beiping) According to sources concerned, Wang Keming's visit and discussions with the authorities here on Sino-Japanese economic cooperation issues yielded largely consistent opinions. As Wang is a financial expert, the authorities here hope that Wang will come forward to take charge of this matter. Wang intends to consider further before making a decision. It is reported that if Wang is willing to come forward to take responsibility, Tianjin and Beiping will form another North China economic organization with a larger scale than the Hebei-Chahar Economic Commission. Its nature will be as an advisory body to the Hebei-Chahar Political Council. If there are no other problems, it may be established in August. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

Yongding River Floods, Strict Flood Control Measures Implemented in All Sections 19

(Beiping) The Lugouqiao telephone reports that due to continuous heavy rains in the upper reaches of the Yongding River in Huailai and Xuanhua, Chahar Province, the water level at the Lugouqiao Huilongmiao water gauge had suddenly risen to one zhang and six chi (approximately 5.3 meters), fortunately without causing a disaster. On the morning of the 11th, the river water gradually dropped to twelve chi. However, the heavy rains in the areas bordering Shanxi and Chahar in the upper reaches have not stopped, and mountain torrents have erupted, pouring down rapidly. Tonight, the water gauge has reached a total of one zhang and eight chi. Liu Yufu, director of the Yongding River Affairs Bureau, urgently telegraphed all sections along the river to increase vigilance and flood prevention, and telegraphed the Hebei Construction Department and the North China Water Conservancy Commission to report. According to records, the highest water level recorded during the major flood of the Yongding River in 1934 was one zhang and eight chi and two cun. Today's water level is feared to exceed that trend. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

(Tianjin) At the Lugouqiao section of the Yongding River, the water level rose sharply to eighteen chi on the night of the 11th, with a very rapid current. In the Wuqing section, the water has reached the level of the embankment. The embankments in the Chenjiazui Yubakou area are thin and likely to collapse. The county magistrate is supervising several thousand people to reinforce the embankments. The North Canal has also flooded due to the backflow of Yongding River water into the Beicang gate, with the water increasing by six chi, submerging all docks on both banks. The water level is still rising continuously. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

South Canal Water Level Continues to Rise 20

(Tianjin) The South Canal water level continues to rise. The River Affairs Bureau sent letters to the counties along the river, urging them to quickly gather laborers to prevent danger. The Machang Jiuxuan Gate water dam was immediately dismantled to release the water. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Tianjin City Prevents Floods 21

(Tianjin) The Tianjin Flood Prevention Association, organized by the Municipal Works Bureau, is preventing flooding of the municipal river. It has also formed five flood prevention teams, each with twenty members. The inaugural meeting will be held on the 15th. Five thousand yuan has been allocated to repair the dikes of the municipal river. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Second Closure of Yaodi Still Requires Consultation on Methods 22

(Hankou) Liu Shoupeng and Yang Silian discussed the method of the second closure of Yaodi with Fan Xixu and others in Shagang. Engineering personnel proposed three methods: 1. Using a "wan yue" style closure. 2. Using 6,000 cubic meters of boulders as closure material. 3. Blocking the water dam at Xiongjiaqiao. However, none are certain. However, in principle, it was decided to comply with the telegram orders of the Economic Commission and the Provincial Government and continue to proceed. Most of the construction workers have been dismissed. They will be reassembled after the method is determined. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Water Rises in the Upper Reaches of the Yellow River 23

(Jinan) The water has risen in the upper reaches of the Yellow River today. Kong Xiangrong arrived at Haikou. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Yanqing Bandit Gang Collapses and Retreats 24

(Beiping) The Huairou telephone reports that the Huangsha Society occurred near the Yongning and Sihai towns in Yanqing County. After defeating the Gubeikou International Police team, over three hundred Japanese troops stationed in Gubeikou went to suppress the bandits some days ago and sent two planes to bomb them, collapsing and defeating the bandits. A total of over three hundred people were killed or injured. The Japanese troops suppressing the bandits arrived in Huairou from Chengning along the Guanda River in the afternoon and are scheduled to take military vehicles back to Gubeikou for their original defense tonight. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Lincheng Coal Mine Temporarily Postpones Resumption of Work 25

(Beiping) The Jilincheng Coal Mine in Hebei Province was flooded earlier and has been shut down for a long time. The Hebei Provincial Government, considering it a pity to abandon it, had the Construction Department formulate a plan to resume work and submit it to the Political Council for review. The Council then handed it over to the Construction Committee for deliberation. It is reported that the review resulted in a decision to postpone the matter because the resumption of work would require considerable funds and there would be many difficulties. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

Sichuan Province Organizes a People's Food Relief Committee 26

(Chongqing) There has been a prolonged drought in Sichuan with no rain. Crops have withered and died. Food is scarce. The price of rice per dou has risen from 2.34 yuan to 4.56 yuan. The people are extremely alarmed. The Xingying and the Provincial Government, for the sake of relief, specially formed the Sichuan People's Food Relief Committee, scheduled to be established tomorrow. It will start purchasing food from Hubei, Jiujiang, and Wuhu as soon as possible to transport to Sichuan for relief. The funds are set at two million yuan, and the losses will be compensated by the Provincial Government with three hundred thousand yuan. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

Traffic Resumes in Southern Hunan 27

(Changsha) The Provincial Government received a telegram from Luo Lin, commander of the Hengzhou Garrison, reporting that traffic has resumed in the Southern Hunan area and that order in the counties is as usual. (Special dispatch from the 12th)

(Nanjing) Because the affairs of the Ministry are very busy, all senior officials went to the Ministry to work on the 12th, even though it was a regular Sunday holiday. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

County and Municipal Administrative Training Institute Graduates Trainees; President Jiang Gives Instructions and Awards Certificates 34

(Nanjing) The fourth class of over one hundred trainees from the County and Municipal Administrative Training Institute of the Ministry of Interior held a graduation ceremony at the Military Academy at 9:00 AM on the 12th. Over four hundred people participated, including President Jiang, heads of various ministries and commissions, chairmen of various provincial governments, and all the trainees. After the ceremony was presided over by Jiang Zuobin, the director of the Institute, President Jiang gave instructions, with the main points of the speech being: (1) During this time of national crisis, officials responsible for local administration, although civil servants, should also be proficient in military affairs in order to cope with extraordinary events. (2) They should promote Chinese virtues and practice benevolence towards the people in order to win their hearts. Only when the people and the government become one can the country be strong. (3) The trainees should do their best to instill what they have learned in Beijing into the people so that they can understand the central government's policies, which will have a multiplier effect on the promotion of national policies in the future. Deputy President Kong then gave instructions. After the speeches, President Jiang personally awarded certificates. The ceremony ended at 11:00 AM. At noon, all personnel of the Training Institute and officials above the rank of senior official of the Ministry of Interior gathered at the Youth Cafeteria for a meal. The county magistrates of the fifth class will arrive in Beijing for training in early August. (Central News Agency dispatch from the 12th)

President Jiang Orders the Hubei Peasant Bank to Allocate Funds for Relief to Various Counties on the Borders of Three Provinces 35

(Nanjing) President Jiang, considering that the people in the counties of Sishui, Shifeng, Xianfeng, Laifeng, Longshan, etc., on the borders of Hubei, Hunan, and Sichuan, have been destitute after banditry, specially ordered the Hubei Peasant Bank in Hankou to quickly allocate 200,000 yuan for relief. (Special dispatch from the 11th)

Current Affairs Commentary

On the Issue of Factory Inspections in the International Settlement 41

— Li

The direct purpose of the state in enacting factory laws is to improve the treatment of workers and reduce labor-management disputes. The indirect purpose is to promote industrial safety and develop the national economy. This indispensable legal code in industrial administration is of great significance. However, if there is only a factory law without the implementation of factory inspections to assess the extent and scope of the factory law's implementation, then the legislative purpose of the factory law cannot be achieved. Therefore, after promulgating factory laws, all countries follow up with the promulgation of factory inspection laws to establish a factory inspection system. Our country's factory inspection law was promulgated on January 10th of the 20th year of the Republic (1931) and implemented on October 1st of the same year. Currently, over twenty provinces and cities have implemented factory inspections in accordance with the law. However, the Shanghai settlement area, which has the most factories in the country, has yet to implement it. This is truly regrettable.

Before the implementation of factory inspection laws, the Ministry of Industry of our country invited experts from the International Labour Office, Mr. Pone and Mr. Anderson, to China to assist and discuss factory inspection methods with the Shanghai settlement authorities. In November of the 20th year of the Republic, the Ministry of Industry again invited representatives from the Shanghai Municipal Government, the Public Concession, and the French Concession Municipal Council to hold informal meetings to continue discussions. At that time, two principles were determined: (1) There should only be one set of labor regulations in each industrial area of Shanghai. (2) The implementation of these regulations should be carried out by inspection personnel, whose actions should be uniform and not vary. Soon after, a third informal meeting was held, and three principles were determined: (1) The Shanghai Public Concession and French Concession authorities agreed to employ factory inspectors trained and recommended by the Chinese government to inspect all factories within their respective boundaries. These inspectors would be supervised by inspectors from the central inspection office at any time. (2) Factory inspectors in the Public Concession and French Concession should report the results of their inspections and any difficulties encountered to the Chinese government and the Public Concession and French Concession authorities on a regular basis. (3) Factory inspectors in the Shanghai Public Concession and French Concession should hold monthly meetings to exchange opinions and discuss solutions to any issues that need to be addressed. However, the board of directors of the Public Concession believed that these two resolutions had not been formally approved and specially convened a special meeting of taxpayers to amend Article 34 of the Yangjingbang land charter attachment to obtain the necessary authority to order factories to obtain licenses before establishing an inspection agency within the concession and implementing a set of industrial regulations that would apply equally to Chinese and foreign factories. Regardless of whether the special meeting of taxpayers had the authority to amend the Yangjingbang land charter and its attachments, even if they really had the authority to change the nature of the concession, this approach would not only allow foreign nationals in China to take advantage of the fact that our country's legal rights had not been fully recovered to apply their own country's laws, but also prevent Chinese citizens residing in the foreign settlements within our own territory from applying our own country's laws. Would this not be a major disregard for our country's legislative power? Therefore, the Municipal Government authorities protested, and citizen groups rose up in opposition. The concession authorities abandoned the original plan due to this backlash. Subsequently, although the central government twice sent representatives to previous International Labor Conferences to request the International Labour Office's assistance in persuading representatives of various governments to mediate, it still had no effect. Recently, the Shanghai Municipal Government and the Public Concession authorities consulted several times before finally reaching a draft agreement of nine articles on the 25th of last month. The content of the agreement included four main points: (1) Our country authorizes the Municipal Council to establish a factory inspection office in the concession to implement factory inspections. (2) The inspectors are to be appointed in equal numbers by the Chinese authorities and the Municipal Council. (3) In cases of violations of laws and regulations that require the enforcement of Chinese factory laws, lawsuits should be filed with the court. (4) The Municipal Council must submit a report to the Chinese authorities. From these four main points, it appears that the right to inspect factories in the concession nominally still belongs to our country, and that the concession is to inspect factories in accordance with our country's factory laws. However, in terms of actual authority, our side has made significant concessions. Unexpectedly, this agreement has encountered further complications at the recent meeting of the Consular Body. The Consular Body demanded a narrowing of the scope of application of the agreement, seeking to exempt factories of countries with consular jurisdiction from inspection procedures. This is a major blow to the issue of factory inspections because the main significance of factory inspections is to protect labor, and the workers in foreign factories in Shanghai are all Chinese. They especially need the protection of the government. If factory inspections exclude foreign factories, then this measure will not only have little effect but will also put Chinese-owned factories at a disadvantage in competition with foreign factories. Therefore, the equal inspection of foreign factories is something our side must fight for. However, various countries are still adhering to the unequal treaties of the past. If there is no new development in nationalist diplomacy, this smaller issue of factory inspections in the Public Concession will likely be very difficult to completely resolve.

The mission of the commercial officers is to open up new markets, investigate general commercial conditions, and dump Japanese goods to compete with Britain and the United States for markets. It has now requested an overseas economic investigation fee of 600,000 yen from the national policy budget in order to correct the worldwide commercial nationalization alliance against Japan. In the 12th year of Showa (1937), it plans to send three investigation teams to South America, the South Seas, and Africa to investigate immigration issues, market transplantations, and development. Travel Notes in Japan (1) 66

— Our Correspondents Hu Zhongchi and Hu Yizang

Not long ago, we spent more than fifty days traveling to Japan. In addition to sightseeing, we visited many public and private institutions in administration, industry, and culture, and visited several grand expositions. We also visited our country's embassy and consulates in Japan to investigate the lives of overseas Chinese. We received sincere hospitality from Japanese friends everywhere, and in several major cities, we were cared for by our country's ambassadors, consuls, and Japanese friends as if we were family. We will never forget this warmth.

During this trip, we admired the beautiful island scenery, the brilliant Yamato art, marveled at the magnificent urban construction, the flourishing industrial civilization, and admired the diligent national spirit and the orderly political order. At the same time, we also sympathized with the suffering of farmers and workers and lamented that a few ambitious people were sowing the seeds of war in the hearts of peace-loving people. Those ambitious people, on the one hand, advocated war thought, and on the other hand, controlled most of the country's productivity, and massively manufactured murderous weapons—tanks, cannons, battleships, submarines, guns, bullets, and even chemical weapons and poison gas—in order to make their empire monopolize East Asia and dominate the world.

Under today's international situation, this attempt is obviously an unattainable dream. However, this dream not only makes the majority of the people in their country sacrifice their welfare in vain but also causes great suffering to our nation. For the sake of our own nation, and for the sake of the majority of the people of the "friendly country," we Chinese must unite as one and use the power of solidarity to awaken those ambitious people from their dream. First of all, we should get rid of the unnecessary fear of the "powerful neighbor" and inspire national self-confidence. Historical facts teach our nation: "We do not need to be afraid of neighboring countries, nor should we be afraid of neighboring countries." After this practical observation, we feel that the above belief is unshakable.

Now we are writing down the various impressions we have gained during this trip according to our itinerary, hoping that these messy materials can help some Chinese people understand Japan.

I. Police Network and Tariff Barriers

The morning sun had just shone on the Huishan Wharf of the Japan Mail Steamship Company. We carried our simple luggage and took a car there to catch the "Nagasaki Maru," which was scheduled to depart at 9:00 AM.

As soon as we arrived at the pier, the "red caps" carried our suitcases onto the ship. We were about to follow, but a Chinese constable standing at the entrance of the steps stopped us. He pointed to the words on the wooden sign next to him and said to us, "Please wait until about 8:30 to exchange your tickets at the pier before going up." We had no choice but to stand there and wait. Later, the pier was already crowded with people before four staff members from the shipping company sat down at two small tables to exchange tickets for passengers one by one. We filled out the passenger registration form, which had many items, exchanged our tickets, boarded the ship, and there were less than fifteen minutes left before departure. In Chinese society, we have always lived a leisurely and casual life. Coming into contact with the orderly and strict spirit of Japan's transportation organization for the first time, which emphasizes time economy, we really felt a little out of place.

After boarding the ship, we should have been able to relax a little, right? However, the Japanese Imperial Government's network of detectives densely spread across its own merchant ships prevented us from relaxing. We were thoroughly questioned by four plainclothes detectives on the ship, one after another. They not only inquired about our age, place of origin, address, and the route of this trip but also investigated when and in what school we graduated and what purpose we had in going to those places in Japan. They recorded all of our answers on large stacks of paper. We wanted to prove our words by taking out various letters of introduction we were carrying with us, but they were not afraid of trouble and copied even the most ordinary ones. We are Chinese news reporters, and it is no wonder that they paid special attention to our travels throughout Japan. However, many ordinary Japanese merchants on the same ship were also carefully questioned. We personally saw a Japanese vegetable merchant not only subjected to a long period of questioning but even a lecture record of a confectionery training class that he took out to prove his legitimate occupation was copied from beginning to end by the detective, taking a full half hour. This thorough spirit is not so much a commendable feature of the Japanese police system as it is a reflection of the underlying anxiety within Japan. Indeed, we have heard that despite the meticulousness of the Japanese police system, there are still many Communists secretly active in the country. Red propaganda is often found in some public institutions in Tokyo, and no matter how hard the detectives try, they cannot find the source of the propaganda.

Many of the first-class cabins on the Nagasaki Maru are reserved for civil servants who interrogate passengers. In addition to military and police personnel, there are also inspectors and quarantine officers from the Japanese Customs. We also felt the strictness of Japan's tariff barriers on the ship. Notices with "Passenger Attention" were posted on the ship, stating that any passenger carrying more than 100 cigarettes or more than 50 cigars when landing would be penalized according to the tax evasion regulations. Before the ship even entered Japanese waters, the "kyuji" (tea boy) on the ship brought two forms and asked us to fill them out. One was a passenger's report on tobacco for personal use, and the other was a passenger's report on carried items. We had a newly purchased small camera, and because the "kyuji" said that it would inevitably cause trouble at customs, we had to scrape off some of the paint on the camera and write our names on the outside of the leather bag to make it look like an old camera. We also had two small baskets of oranges, which were given to us by relatives. We heard that not even one orange or similar fruit could be brought ashore, so we finally had to throw away most of the remaining oranges on the ship.

The Nagasaki Maru sailed for a day and night, bringing us to the border of Japan. The sea view composed of the scattered islands along the coast of Kyushu as seen from the deck is very beautiful. However, when we saw the announcement from the Nagasaki Fortress Headquarters posted on the ship, we had a different feeling. The announcement drew a schematic diagram of the fortress area, warning passengers not to photograph, sketch, or record within this area. We knew that we had entered the heavily guarded Japanese military zone.

Page 8

Germany's Recognition of Austria: Three Main Principles, Respect for Independence, Non-Interference in Internal Affairs; Austria Promulgates New Laws to Curb National Socialist Party Activities; The Issue of Royal Restoration is Within the Scope of Internal Affairs 67

(Vienna) The agreement established between Germany and Austria is conditional on Germany's recognition of three main principles: (1) Austrian independence, (2) Germany's non-interference in Austrian internal affairs, and (3) the activities of the National Socialist Party being an internal affair and not a subject for negotiation. Observers have declared that the mutual relations and economic development of Germany and Austria should be based on these principles. (Havas, 11th)

(Vienna) Responsible officials have declared that the interim measures signed between Germany and Austria will not have any impact on Austria's internal affairs. The Austrian government has decided to strictly curb the activities of the National Socialist Party and will promulgate a new law today called the "National Security" Law. All means used to punish rebellious acts and the German-Austrian merger movement shall be specified in detail. As for the restoration of the old Habsburg royal family, it should be regarded as a purely internal matter and not within the scope of diplomacy. In short, the political program determined by the late Prime Minister Dollfuss will continue to be followed without change, and the principles contained in this program should also be endorsed by Germany. (Havas, 11th)

Reorganization of the Austrian Cabinet to Gain German Favor; Pro-German Faction Appointed Minister Without Portfolio; National Socialist Schmidt Takes Charge of Foreign Affairs 68

(Vienna) It is rumored that after the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, the Austrian cabinet will be reorganized in order to gain German favor. (Havas, 11th)

(Vienna) After the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, the discussion of reorganizing the Austrian cabinet was implemented last night. Dr. Hoste Laue has been appointed as Minister Without Portfolio, and the position of Foreign Minister, originally held concurrently by Prime Minister Schuschnigg, has also been changed to be held by Schmidt. Hoste Laue is currently 54 years old, a Catholic, and has always advocated pro-German sentiments. He holds a doctorate from the University of Monk City in Germany and once served as the director of the National Archives. Schmidt is currently 37 years old, served as an attaché at the Embassy in France, and has been working in the Presidential Palace since 1928, originally as the secretary to President Miklas, and then as the Deputy Director of the Civil Service Department until now. (Havas, 12th)

Bulgaria to Lift Sanctions Against Italy from Tomorrow 69

Bulgaria's capital: The government has decided to lift sanctions against Italy from midnight on the 14th of this month. (Havas, 12th)

European Situation Changes Rapidly: Italy, Germany, and Austria Form a Group to Resist the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact; Contents of the German-Austrian Friendship Agreement Announced; London Relieved, Paris Remains Silent for the Time Being 70

(Vienna) The German-Austrian friendship agreement was published in the government gazette today. According to the agreement, Austria recognizes itself as a Germanic country, and Germany also recognizes Austria's complete autonomy. The two governments will also create the necessary environment for implementing German-Austrian consultation in several different ways. However, the gazette also stated that the Rome Protocols of 1934 and 1936 will not be changed due to the new agreement. Therefore, the agreement has opened the way for an alliance between Italy, Austria, and Germany, connecting the North Sea to the Mediterranean Sea to resist the Franco-Soviet Mutual Assistance Pact. (National Telegram, 11th)

(London) Austrian Prime Minister Schuschnigg and German Propaganda Minister Goebbels simultaneously read the same communiqué in their respective capitals last night, broadcasting it to the entire country via radio. The communiqué stated that Austria and Germany believe that the establishment of a friendship agreement between them will ease the tense situation in Europe. The terms of the agreement are as follows:

(1) Germany recognizes Austria's full sovereignty.

(2) Each country agrees not to directly or indirectly interfere in the other's internal political development, including the issue of Austrian National Socialism.

(3) Austria intends to maintain a special policy towards Germany in accordance with the basic principle of Austria recognizing itself as a Germanic country, so as not to disturb the Rome Protocol of 1934 and the additional documents of 1936, and the status of Austria, Italy, and Hungary as parties to this document.

The communiqué indicated that the agreement would be completed with various separate plans. It is also reported that both parties have satisfactorily agreed on the amnesty issue, and each country's newspapers can be sent to the other's country. As for economic adjustment measures, the main condition will be the exchange of goods. (Reuters, 12th)

(Rome) All of Italy is very satisfied to hear the news of the establishment of the German-Austrian friendship agreement. Italy has a close relationship with the negotiations of this agreement, but initially did not expect it to be so quickly successful. Germany's recognition of Austrian independence has always been the only difficulty between Italy and Germany. Now that this difficulty has been removed, Italy and Germany can closely unite. It is expected that the most recent consequences of the agreement will be:

(1) At the future Locarno Conference, Italy will refuse to participate if Germany is not allowed to join.

(2) Italy will abandon its plan to reform the "Stresa Front."

The authorities deny that Italian Prime Minister Mussolini has a plan to restore the Four-Power Pact of Italy, Britain, France, and Germany, because although sanctions against Italy have been lifted, Italy's wishes have not been fully satisfied and it is still unable to participate in general European cooperation. (Reuters, 12th)

(London) London political circles are very relieved to hear the news of the success of German-Austrian friendship, because the agreement will greatly change Germany's attitude towards Austria. It is expected that Germany will conduct large-scale economic activities in Austria, creating a close relationship between the two countries. (Reuters, 12th)

(Paris) Political circles here have remained silent about the new developments between Austria and Germany yesterday, and the authorities have not made any criticisms. However, it is generally believed that Germany will pay attention to other issues in the future, such as the Danzig issue and colonial issues. (Reuters, 12th)

Italy and Austria Exchange Telegrams to Guarantee the Promotion of Friendship Between the Two Countries 71

(Rome) Yesterday, Italian Prime Minister Mussolini and Austrian Prime Minister Schuschnigg exchanged telegrams as a guarantee of friendship between the two countries. Schuschnigg announced the signing of the new German-Austrian friendship agreement, stating that the agreement aims to make a very effective new contribution to the work of peace. Mussolini replied that all those who cherish pacifism must be satisfied and celebrate the agreement, which is a significant step towards European reconstruction. (Reuters, 12th)

(Rome) After signing the agreement with the German authorities, Austrian Prime Minister Schuschnigg immediately telegraphed Italian Prime Minister Mussolini, saying, "I would like to take this opportunity to express my wish that the friendship between the two sides will continue to grow, and I agree with you completely, and will closely cooperate in accordance with the Rome Protocols established between Italy, Austria, and Hungary on March 17, 1934, and March 24 of this year." The Prime Minister immediately replied by telegraph, also mentioning the Rome Protocol, and said, "The agreement you have just signed is of great importance to the reconstruction of Europe and the Danube region." (Havas, 12th)

Rome Expresses Satisfaction: The Estrangement Between Germany and Austria is Completely Removed 72

(Rome) After the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, semi-official circles here expressed satisfaction, saying that this agreement was discussed by Prime Minister Mussolini and Austrian Prime Minister in the town of Gameda more than a month ago. Official officials also added criticism, saying that the most satisfactory aspects of this agreement are two points: (1) German leader Hitler made a declaration on May 21, 1935, stating his willingness to respect Austrian independence, and this time he reiterated this statement; (2) Austria still adheres to the Rome Protocols established by Italy, Austria, and Hungary on March 17, 1934, and March 24 of this year, and Germany also supports this. (Havas, 11th)

Polish People Welcome, but Worry About Expansion to the East 73

Warsaw: People here have expressed their welcome for the German-Austrian agreement, believing that this is the foundation for an understanding between Italy and Germany. Responsible officials also said that Poland has had the desire to approach Italy and Germany for a year, and this trend will inevitably become stronger. What the Ministry of Foreign Affairs has been working on in the past is to improve relations with Italy while not offending Italy. If Italy, Germany, and Poland cooperate in the future, Germany and Italy can take active actions in the Balkan Peninsula. However, some people in political circles have slightly different views. They believe that if Germany's power to expand outward gains the support of Italy and Austria in the south, it will inevitably turn to the east, damaging Poland. Judging from Germany's recent attitude towards the Free City of Danzig, it can be known that this statement is not false. (Havas, 12th)

Austrian Factions' Views: A Portion of the Catholic Party Holds Doubts; The Patriotic Front Takes a Vigilant Attitude 74

(Vienna) People from all walks of life have different opinions on the agreement established between Germany and Austria, but they generally express satisfaction with the appointment of Hoste Laue as Minister Without Portfolio and Schmidt as Foreign Minister. It is said that Hoste Laue has always advocated cultural rapprochement with Germany, but does not agree with the merger of Germany and Austria politically. Here is an analysis of the views of various parties on the German-Austrian agreement: Although the Catholic Party is divided into those who tend towards Germany and those who tend towards the Vatican, they all have doubts about the practical effects of this agreement. Members of the Internal Guard generally support the agreement in principle, but say that it is still difficult to reach a conclusion at this time. The Patriotic Defense League advocates taking a vigilant attitude for the time being. As for the royalists, they regret that the agreement did not simultaneously make a decision on the restoration of the old Habsburg royal family, believing that the merger of Germany and Austria could be stopped after the restoration of the Habsburg royal family, which would be more powerful than the promises that German leader Hitler could provide. "Since the issue of Austrian restoration is outside the scope of the agreement, the issue of the form of government is purely within the scope of internal affairs, and the German government has probably recognized this." Therefore, the royalists will intensify the restoration movement. In addition, pro-German factions who are not members of the National Socialist Party also express satisfaction. However, members of the National Socialist Party are deeply puzzled and very frustrated as to why leader Hitler refused to provide assistance. (Havas, 12th)

Italian Prime Minister Mussolini Prepares to Propose a Startling Plan: No Intention to Restore the Stresa Front; Foreign Policy Based on Pro-German Sentiment; Advocates Concluding a Six-Power Pact Including Russia and Poland 75

(Rome) Since the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, responsible officials here believe that Italy's foreign policy in the future should aim at two goals: cooperation among the major European powers and the issue of the Danube River region. Prime Minister Mussolini is currently on vacation and will propose a startling plan as soon as he returns. However, although Italy is willing to re-participate in various European issues, it has no intention of restoring the Stresa Front, because the three countries of Britain, France, and Italy established this front to prevent Germany from interfering in Austrian internal affairs. Now that the German-Austrian agreement has been established, there is no risk of interference in Austrian internal affairs, so there is no need to restore the Stresa Front. If the signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty hold a meeting in Beijing in the future without Germany's participation, it would be like restoring this front, which is not what Italy wants. Responsible officials also believe that the reason why the German-Austrian agreement was established early was to enable Italy to decide its position on the Locarno Conference in a timely manner and announce it to the world. In short, Italy's current foreign policy is based on the friendship between Italy and Germany. If the Western European peace plan proves impossible to realize, this friendly relationship should be further enhanced and strengthened. At that time, the cooperation between Italy and Germany will be sufficient to deal with everything, and there is no need to ask for anything else, nor is it necessarily impossible. However, Italy should still propose a new European pact plan at this time, advocating that Italy, Germany, Britain, France, Poland, and Soviet Russia conclude a six-power pact. In the minds of Italian politicians, it is necessary for European countries to cooperate with each other according to their strengths and weaknesses, which is a necessary condition for organizing Europe. As for the issue of the Danube River region, the Little Entente countries originally provided guarantees for Austrian independence, but since Italy, Austria, and Hungary established the Rome Protocols in March 1934 and March of this year, and the German-Austrian agreement was established yesterday, this guarantee is of no use. Although the Little Entente countries can establish an agreement with Austria in the future, in fact, they must negotiate with Italy and Germany at the same time. After the establishment of the German-Austrian agreement, Germany can be considered to have joined the Rome Protocols previously established by Italy, Austria, and Hungary. According to this protocol, any signatory country often consults other signatory countries before conducting diplomatic negotiations with other countries. In addition, although the Little Entente countries can join the Rome Protocols, they should do so separately. In a nutshell, Austria is in an intermediate position between the Little Entente countries and Italy and Germany, and it is also the medium for Italy and Germany to enter Eastern and Southern Europe. (Havas, 12th)

Italy Refuses to Attend the Locarno Treaty Conference: Mediterranean Mutual Assistance Should be Abolished First, and Invitation of Germany to Participate is a Prerequisite 78

The Italian government now replied that Italy is always prepared to make a strong contribution to peace, but at present it has to pay attention to certain obligations in the Mediterranean, which are obstacles to its participation in the meeting. Furthermore, the Italian government believes that Germany should also be invited to participate in the initial stages of the Locarno Conference, because the absence of one of the signatory countries of the Locarno Treaty will not only fail to clarify the current situation, but will instead increase disputes. (London) Since Germany and Austria have already established an agreement in advance, and Italy has refused to participate in the Locarno Conference (scheduled to be held in Beijing on the 22nd of this month) because Germany has not received an invitation, officials here have commented one after another, believing that Germany's recognition of Austria's complete sovereignty may have obtained important exchange conditions from Italy. The current question is whether Britain and France can meet the various demands made by Italy, that is, whether the mutual assistance measures established by Britain with various countries along the Mediterranean coast last year can be abolished, whether the Locarno Conference can immediately invite Germany to participate, or whether Britain, France, and Belgium will hold a meeting to discuss a Western European defense pact and disregard Germany and Italy. All of this must be decided. Regarding this level, officials believe that the future Locarno Conference should adopt a compromise approach, that is, Britain, France, and Belgium will hold a meeting on the one hand, and negotiate with Germany and Italy on the other hand, so that when the conference reaches the second stage (that is, the negotiations on the overall European situation), Germany and Italy will come out to participate. According to this, the experts of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs should thoroughly study the past events of the Locarno Treaty issue, and prepare for the meeting on the level of Italy's promise to participate. (Havas, 11th)

(Rome) The Italian government has not yet submitted a reply to the invitation to the Locarno Conference, and Germany and Austria have already established an agreement. The so-called sanctions not only refer to purely sanction measures, but also to various measures with a sanction nature, such as the mutual assistance measures established by Britain with various countries along the Mediterranean coast last year, which should also be abolished; (2) The French government has declared the mutual assistance measures previously established by Britain and France invalid, which Italy is very satisfied with; (3) Italy is currently working to reconcile the attitudes of Germany and Italy; (4) Italy wants Germany to participate in the Locarno Conference. (Havas, 11th)

A Comprehensive View of Japan's Economic Policies Toward China: Collaboration in Name, Aggression in Reality, Seizing Resources and Actively Preparing for War 80

Special Article from the China Alliance News Agency: Japan's Ambassador to China, Kawagoe Shigeru, has been in China for less than a month. He has expressed his views on Sino-Japanese issues in several talks, mainly stating that to adjust Sino-Japanese relations, one should start with economic collaboration. First, in North China, a special zone between Japan and "Manchukuo," Japan should provide economic assistance, invest in North China railways, implement rural collaboration and guidance, and investigate and develop mines. On the surface, this diplomatic policy seems more moderate than "bomb diplomacy with fists." However, in essence, it is the most vicious plan to annex the entire North China, following the increase of troops and in coordination with the troop increase policy. This is because Japan's economic policy toward North China is based on pouring all efforts into preparing for a major war. The content of this policy is: (1) Seizing military raw material resources; (2) Placing existing railways and highways under Japanese control, preparing to transform them into military routes when war breaks out; (3) Constructing roads with military significance. Kawagoe's diplomatic ambition coincides with this content. Who says it is a symbol of Japan's mitigated aggression against China? Now, let's cite specific facts to further expose the role of so-called economic collaboration. First, let's talk about the railway issue. Currently, the most actively pursued project in the Japanese plan is the construction of the Cangshi Railway. Once this railway is completed, it will have three major functions: (1) It can transport coal from Shanxi directly to Tianjin or Qingdao; (2) It can facilitate the exploitation of resources along the line; (3) It can be used to transport troops from Qingdao to Shanxi and Suiyuan. Another planned project is the extension of the PingSui Railway, connecting it with Chifeng in the puppet Rehe Province via Zhangbei and Dolun. Needless to say, this project has even greater military significance, as it can provide another shortcut for transporting military supplies and attacking Outer Mongolia. In addition, the BeiNing Railway and the PingSui Railway are actually already under its control because of direct or indirect relations with Japan. Then, there is the issue of assisting rural reconstruction, the main point of which is to encourage the cultivation of cotton. Because Japan is an industrial country, cotton is the main raw material for the textile industry. However, Japan is very lacking in this regard and has always imported it from India and the Americas. If a conflict occurs with Britain and the the United States, this important source may be cut off, putting the textile industry at risk of fundamental bankruptcy. Therefore, the military and capitalists regard North China as the target for cotton production and also plan to establish natural research institutes to improve cotton production, making it more suitable for the needs of Osaka textile industry capitalists. However, Japan's purpose in assisting and encouraging North China farmers to grow cotton is not limited to this, because its assistance and encouragement will allow it to control China's cotton resources. As a result, China's "flickering candle"-like textile industry will inevitably face even more serious difficulties. Third, there is the issue of developing mineral resources. According to surveys, the coal reserves in North China account for 80% of China's total reserves. Shanxi Province alone has more than 12.7 million tons, and among these more than 12 million tons, 3.64 million tons are anthracite, which is one of the raw materials most needed by Japan's ordinary industries and military industries. Naturally, it is coveting and unwilling to let go. At the same time, it also has a plan to take the British-owned Kailuan Coal Mine into its own hands. On the one hand, it uses the products of the Fushun Company to hit the Kailuan Company's sales market in North China, and on the other hand, it spreads a lot of rumors, which will inevitably lead to Kailuan being ceded to Japan. In addition, there is also the seizure of Chinese coal mining enterprises. Now, companies such as Linyuan and Liujiang have been plundered by it. Speaking of iron, according to surveys, the total reserves in China are 236.854 million tons, and Xuanhua in Chahar alone accounts for 39%. In addition to Xuanhua, there are still 32.424 million tons in Hebei Province and 13.7 million tons in Shandong Province. Japan needs about 2.5 million to 3 million tons of iron every year, most of which depends on foreign countries. Therefore, how can it not want to get involved in the iron ore in the provinces of North China under military and political control? Are these facts not enough to illustrate the true face of the economic diplomacy advocated by Kawagoe? We have already said above that this economic diplomacy is coordinated with the troop increase policy, and the purpose of annexing the entire North China is in the economy, and the purpose of this economy, in addition to selling goods and plundering raw materials, also has the function of preparing for war. The troop increase is to cover up the promotion of this goal. Under the support of the military, Kawagoe came to China to take office amid the voice of increasing troops. The seriousness contained in the so-called economic collaboration is very obvious. "Politics is the concentrated expression of economics." We believe that apart from those with ulterior motives, everyone understands that the so-called economic collaboration is to make North China fall into a completely colonial status.
