The World's Largest Vertical Lift Bridge Completed on the Hudson River: President Roosevelt Presides Over the Ceremony, The Bridge Is Twenty-Three Miles Long and Cost Sixty-Four Million 88

(New York) The government recently built a bridge on the Hudson River in this city, named the "Triborough Bridge" (because Manhattan, the Bronx, and Queens are all connected by it). It is the world's largest vertical lift bridge, which can be raised up to twenty-four meters to allow ships to pass underneath. It is actually divided into four bridges, each paved with high-level roads to connect with each other. The bridge body is twenty-three kilometers long, of which the middle section of the pontoon bridge is four kilometers long, and the bridge surface used for lifting is 420 meters long. The total cost is 64,000,000 US dollars, and part of the cost will be repaid by collecting tolls from passing cars. The bridge has recently been completed, and President Roosevelt will personally preside over the ceremony and deliver a speech, stating that with the progress of culture and the advancement of science, the needs of mankind have also changed accordingly. "Therefore, the government's task lies in guiding these changes. Furthermore, the people need a modern government to replace the old government, just as the people need a new bridge to replace the old pedestrian orange, which is the same reason." (Havas dispatch, 11th)

Good News from the Southern Tour 89

— Special Correspondent Stone Ying

A Glimpse of Jinhua

The train continued south from Xiaoshan. The mountains on both sides undulated, beautifully strange, clear, and lovely. Looking down at the tracks, the green mountains were close by, covered with large and small black stones, very much like a group of frogs jumping and bumping into the train. Near Linpu, in the low-lying areas, there were many tombs, the coffins exposed and shallowly buried on the horizon. The shape of the tombs was slightly rectangular, while those buried on the hills were conical, dense, and tall. In the same area, there were different burial methods, which I had not seen elsewhere. The detestable Feng Shui masters were causing trouble, arbitrarily occupying usable land for the bones of the dead. The drawbacks were the same everywhere. Someone has proposed changing to cremation, which is worth paying attention to.

Passing Zhuji, the hometown of the peerless beauty Xi Shi, a friend sitting with me, because of military transportation, had not bought yesterday's train ticket. Hearing that he was going to miss a commercial appointment, they talked about a certain country's policy of using Chinese to control Chinese, which led them to think of Yue King Goujian's success in using a beauty trap to control the enemy. They hoped that students studying in Japan would not try exotic foods, leading to bringing spies back with them, and also causing some of their compatriots' women to be affected by the outflow of rights and interests. Hearing this, I peered out the window. The towering Zhuji Pagoda stood far away, saluting the travelers, as if representing the beautiful and affectionate Xi Shi, who had not kept the fleeting guests, but only saw them off for a distance, wishing them "Good luck all the way."

Zhuji also has a very famous scenic spot called "Five Waterfalls." On that uniquely steep Five Waterfalls Mountain, a huge, thunder-like roar emanates from the giant waterfall, which cascades down in five folds. Some of the waterfalls are as long as twenty fathoms, with flashes of white light that dazzle the eyes. According to the Ming Dynasty writer Song Lian's records, there were many monkeys on the mountain at that time. When tourists teased them, they would throw rocks, like rain, showing great resistance.

The city of Yiwu is also surrounded by mountains, but it is not like Xiaoshan, with half of it climbing up the hillside. During the Southern Song Dynasty, Zong Ze, who resisted the enemy and killed the invaders, came from here. In the Luoyang area, he repeatedly defeated the Jin soldiers, repeatedly asking Emperor Gaozong to return to Bianliang (the old capital of the Northern Song Dynasty, now Kaifeng, Henan), but Emperor Gaozong did not dare to go. This old man died of anger. In the Mancin Temple in the city, there is still a shrine to him.

Arriving in Jinhua, which is famous for its ham, the terrain is open, and the scenery is relatively prosperous. Even the newly built train station is said to be the best of all the stations on this line. I took a special photo, but was interfered with by the railway police, so it was done in haste, and I did not get the whole picture. After getting off the train and leaving the station, I took a rickshaw into the city. The distance of the journey has a fixed price. Walking along a gravel road for a while, I arrived at the China Travel Service Hostel. Because of the beautiful architecture and facilities, many tourists visiting the Beishan scenic spots stay here.

The prosperous area of the city, from Lotus Well to Xishi Street, is very lively, with the night market open until eight or nine o'clock. There are electric lights and neon lights. The streets are paved with stone, and are more than one fathom wide. The eaves of several shops can almost kiss those on the opposite side. The gravel road from the station leads directly to Zhongshan Park. The park scenery is mostly old houses, with very few flowers, trees, or clean places to rest. The reading room attached to the People's Education Hall displays the Shen Bao, Southeast, and local Zhejiang East newspapers. Because the current situation is sometimes tight and sometimes loose, there are many people vying to read them. Perhaps this is the purpose of visiting the park. In addition, there is a large string of magazines strung together with thick iron wire, very much like the medicine slips in ancient temples. I did not see anyone laboriously flipping through them. It seems that it would not be a reading room without them, but if they are set out, they are afraid that these will disappear. Although the intention is excusable, it ultimately feels very unsightly. Probably everything is being tightened, but the administrator of this room cannot tighten it. Moreover, Jinhua has developed school education and a relatively high cultural level, and needs a more complete public reading room. I think the person in charge must have a plan in mind. Recently, the urban area has been collecting and training volunteer police, with a quota of 200 people. When people voluntarily joined, there were still 100 people. Every morning, they learn "skills" at Bayongtan, and in the evening, they gather in Zhongshan Park to learn "academics" for a total of three hours. The rest of the time, they are engaged in their regular occupations. The results are very good. Judging from their intentions, the purpose is not only to prevent bandits.

Since the opening of the Zhejiang-Jiangxi Railway in Jinhua, customs have become increasingly extravagant. Teahouses and restaurants have sprung up like mushrooms after rain, all hiring several "tea girls" as bait to attract customers. The bad habits of the general population are spreading rapidly. Now, because drug offenses are being dealt with extremely strictly, there is hope of eradication, but the number of opium addicts is still large. Almost everyone has a cigarette in their hand. The Jinhua market has gradually declined since 1934. The main reason is the unprecedented drought that year, which greatly damaged the vitality of the farmers, resulting in a lack of purchasing power. Developed transportation has led to a loss of the position of commercial throughput. Public debt and donations have further increased the burden year by year. The former county magistrate, Li, also raised 100,000 yuan in prize-winning shares for the construction of the Beishan Highway, taking 30% as a bonus and exchanging 70% for share certificates, selling them to households for several hundred yuan, or several tens of yuan each. The country is in a state of crisis and poverty, and the people have reached the point of being squeezed to the bone. Any empty and irrelevant construction, or magnificent government offices, can only serve as embellishments in a prosperous era, and can never alleviate the national crisis in the slightest. This Beishan Highway in Jinhua is only intended to facilitate tourists to visit the scenery of the Beishan Shuanglong Cave and other places, but it has not yet been opened to traffic, but the people are burdened with debt, and everyone is complaining. In addition, the competition between various businesses is also doing its best. For example, the fees charged by the electric light company are more expensive than neighboring counties, and the conditions set are very harsh. Small and medium-sized businesses requested a reduction in fees, but because large businesses are shareholders, they tacitly disapprove, and they can only endure exploitation. In recent years, large and small burdens have accumulated for a long time, and as a result, 60 or 70 companies have declared liquidation and closure. Among them, more than a dozen companies with capital of 10,000 to more than 100,000 yuan could not avoid bankruptcy. At present, only the Jingguang textile industry is doing relatively well, followed by the ham and wine industry, and the rest are mostly struggling to survive.

On the street, I saw a good sign for a "Relief Society Nursery," which attracted the reporter to visit with great pleasure. Mr. Fang, the accountant of the institute, took on the task of receiving me. According to him, "The annual income of the institute, including rent, grain, and donations, is about 8,000 or 9,000 yuan. The salaries of staff, doctors, and wet nurses require 200 yuan per month." In addition to salaries, there is a surplus of 6,000 or 7,000 yuan, which, if used entirely for the poor babies, would be more than sufficient and infinitely beneficial. I saw the statistical table brought by Mr. Fang. This year, a total of 498 babies were received. In addition to those who were adopted (taken to be children, with poor households receiving a monthly subsidy of one yuan for milk and food) and those who were temporarily fostered (only milk, with a monthly subsidy of one and a half yuan), there were still 199 people in the nursery. There were only 16 wet nurses, with an average of 12 or 13 babies per person. When I asked Mr. Fang, I heard from his embarrassed mouth that there were actually only 38 babies. The other 161 little lives probably said goodbye to the world early because they were afraid of being too sorry for such a charitable organization.

Later, under Mr. Fang's leadership, I visited the baby rooms. Each room had several wooden beds, with three or four children sleeping in each bed. Seven or eight out of ten had large heads and thin bodies, and cried weakly. The summer mats on the beds were mostly stained blackish-brown with urine. A strange, musty odor permeated the room, which was probably the slow-acting poisonous gas of those dead babies. Inadequate nutrition was naturally the main culprit. There were also some who were sick in the infirmary. It was said that it was Sunday that day, and there were no doctors to take care of them. Only a few green-headed flies suddenly buzzed and flew around. In the midst of Mr. Fang's statement that "those sent to the infirmary are probably only taken care of in the morning and evening..." I quickly walked away.

Mr. Fang has served in the institute for about 20 years. According to him, the mortality rate of the babies received accounts for 70%, and those who are raised only account for 20% or 30%. Moreover, most of the sources of those who are quickly adopted are "parents are poor" and abandoned due to "a preference for sons over daughters." Therefore, female babies account for more than 90% of those received. Occasionally, when one or two boys are obtained, they are easily adopted. Most of those who adopt female babies are She people, and they also donate money because they do not have a preference for sons over daughters. George Bernard Shaw once visited a nursery in a certain country, and he said something like this: They (the babies) should be made to have a very happy and full meal, and then burned to death in a sweet dream--because this society is not theirs. Although Shaw's words are close to cruelty, the mortality rate of the Jinhua nursery proves that Shaw is exposing the cruel behavior of the old society under a mask for these countless unfortunate little lives, so that true philanthropists can find a way from the root as soon as possible.

Page 10

Li Han-hun and Yu Han-mou's New Expressions on the Situation in Guangdong after their Departure; Li Left Shantou for Hong Kong on the 8th, and Yu Took a Plane from Dayu to Beijing; Chen Jitang Consoled the First Army 90

Guangzhou Correspondence: After the anti-Japanese troops in Guangdong and Guangxi withdrew into Hunan, their military designations were changed to the Anti-Japanese National Salvation Army. Because of this, a few generals had some different opinions. On the 6th of this month, Li Han-hun, the Pacification Commissioner of the Eastern District, first resigned and left Shantou for Hong Kong on the 8th. Li was originally the commander of the Sixth Division. As the Pacification Commissioner of the Eastern District, after the expansion of the army, Li was promoted to Deputy Commander of the Second Army, but he had already lost the position of Commander of the Sixth Division. He only had the nominal titles of Pacification Commissioner of the Eastern District and Deputy Commander of the Army. Therefore, Li was somewhat depressed, so he resolutely left. It is now heard that Chen Jitang has ordered Li Yukun, the Chief of Staff of the Eastern District Pacification Headquarters, to preside over military affairs in Chaozhou and Shantou. Yu Han-mou, the Commander of the First Army, was usually in southern Jiangxi, and his troops were all in southern Jiangxi. On the evening of the 4th, Yu returned to the defense on the pretext of inspecting the troops, and arrived at Huoyu on the 7th. He held a military conference at the headquarters of the First Army. On the morning of the 8th, Yu took a plane to the north. He arrived in Nanchang that afternoon for a short rest, and then went to Beijing from Nanchang to report to the central government on the military and political situation in Guangdong and Guangxi, and to attend the Second Plenary Session of the Kuomintang. After Yu arrived in Beijing, he sent two telegrams to Guangdong, one to Chen Jitang and one to the officers and soldiers of the First Army, advising them to put the overall situation first and unite to resist the enemy. Upon receiving the telegram, Chen Jitang immediately sent Li Heling, the Deputy Director of the General Political Training Department, and Yun Zhenzhong, the staff officer of the First Army stationed in the province, to Huoyu by car on the evening of the 8th to console the officers and soldiers of the First Army. Li and Yun arrived in haste on the 9th and conveyed Chen Jitang's orders to the commanders of the First, Second, and Third Divisions, and instructed them on the plan to consolidate the defense of the Jiangxi-Guangdong border during Yu Han-mou's visit to Beijing. Therefore, there were some rumors outside. The authorities sent Zhang Meixin, the Director of the Deputy Officer's Office of the Headquarters, to the Jiangxi border on the evening of the 9th to meet Li Zhenliang, the Deputy Commander of the First Army, and Mo Xide, the Commander of the First Division, and Ye Zhao, the Commander of the Second Division, and then went to Anyuan to instruct Zhang Ruigui, the Commander of the Third Division. At present, with Yu Han-mou's visit to Beijing, rumors are rife on the Jiangxi-Guangdong border. In order to consolidate the defense of northern Guangdong, the authorities have ordered the Fourth and Fifth Divisions of the Second Army to garrison Shaoguan, Nanxiong, and Shixing. The Thirteenth Division of the Fifth Army, led by Tan Sui, and the Fourteenth Division, led by Chen Zhang, were transferred from Conghua to Yingde on the morning of the 10th to reinforce the defense. However, after Yu and Li left their posts, Huang Tao, the Director of the First Guangdong Arms Factory, Li Jiezhi, the Commander of the Humen Fortress, and Zhang Jian, the Principal of the Military Medical School, also left their posts after Yu and Li on the 10th. (July 11)

Guangdong Planes Heading North 91

The pilots are students of the Sixth Class of the Aviation School; more than 20 other students have left Guangdong. Guangzhou Correspondence: A few days ago, aviation school students in Guangdong province suddenly led fighter planes north. It was found that these students were all students of the Sixth Class of the Aviation School, Classes A and B, assigned to serve in Ding Jixu's Second Air Squadron and Ao Qingyuan's Fifth Air Squadron. The Second Squadron was stationed in Guangzhou, and the Fifth Squadron was stationed in Conghua. During routine training on the morning of the 2nd of this month, seven trainees from the Fifth Squadron, Huang Zhigang, Cai Zhichang, Tan Zhuoli, Luo Chengye, Ma Weidong, and Liu Zhiying, took four Yugoslavian fighter planes and followed Squadron Leader Gu Pengnian to practice aerial combat. Unexpectedly, shortly after taking off, the four planes carrying Huang and others flew straight towards the North River. After Squadron Deputy Gu Pengnian noticed this, he immediately flew back to the Conghua squadron headquarters to report. Squadron Leader Ao Qingyuan then went to the provincial capital in person to ask Air Force Commander Huang Guangrui to punish him, and requested that planes be sent to track and intercept them. While this was being investigated, Ding Jixu's Second Air Squadron also reported that three second lieutenant pilots, Huang Jugu, Cen Zeliu, and Liao Muke, had each flown a fighter plane to the north in the morning, and had not returned to the squadron. The Air Force Command believed that the Sixth Class graduate pilots who had hijacked the planes from Guangdong belonged to the Second Squadron, and that Squadron Leader Ding Jixu should be held responsible. Ding Jixu and Zhou Yuwen, the Second Squadron's chief mechanic, were immediately detained for investigation. At the same time, Huang Pulun, the Deputy Squadron Leader of the Fifth Squadron, was also detained for questioning. After a detailed interrogation, Huang Pulun has been released, and Zhou Yuwen has also been allowed to move freely within the Air Force Command. As for Ding Jixu, his responsibility is greater, and he has been transferred to the Special Room near the police affairs section on the second floor of the Gendarmerie Headquarters. In recent days, Air Force colleagues and their families have come to visit him. If a thorough investigation reveals that there is nothing else, he should be released during the day. However, since the plane hijacking incident, the Air Force Command has immediately been placed under martial law. All officers and pilots are not allowed to leave their posts without reason, and special attention is paid to outsiders entering the unit. Visits from outsiders are declined, and the Adjutant's Office has produced a new blue badge, which will be issued from the 15th of this month to prevent spies from infiltrating. The previously issued square badges will be invalid from the 22nd of this month. It is heard that in addition to the planes that have already headed north, there are currently six air squadrons in Guangdong, and two new squadrons, the Seventh and Eighth, have been expanded. He Jingwei has been appointed as the Commander of the Seventh Squadron, with Deng Qiang as the Deputy Commander. Guo Hanting has been appointed as the Commander of the Eighth Squadron, with Zhou Bingming as the Deputy Commander. They were formally established on the 8th. (July 10)

Japanese Joint Fleet: 72 Ships to Arrive in Xiamen; 60,000 Officers and Soldiers in Total; Japanese Ships Constantly Practicing between Taiwan, Xiamen, and Shantou 92

Xiamen Correspondence: The main force of the Japanese First Fleet and Second Fleet, with 72 ships and 60,000 officers and sailors, led by Joint Fleet Commander Takahashi, arrived in Taiwan on the 27th of last month and berthed in Keelung and Kaohsiung. After the 1st of this month, they set sail and cruised in the Japanese-controlled areas of Southeast Asia, and are scheduled to sail to Xiamen on August 1, where they will anchor for five days before sailing elsewhere. During the period of anchoring in Xiamen, sailors will land in Xiamen and Gulangyu for sightseeing. Because there are 60,000 people, Japanese merchants here are preparing to take this opportunity to do business. The empty shops on Longtou Street in Gulangyu and other city streets have been temporarily rented by Japanese merchants, who will open toy stores, antique stores, and gambling arcades. At the same time, they will print postcards of Xiamen scenery for sale. The scenery collected includes 16 types such as the Xiamen Naval Base Command, the Xiamen Naval Aviation Office, the Asahi Gakuin, the Taiwan Guild, and the Japanese Consulate. Taiwanese are also actively preparing a grand welcome. According to reports, before 1924, when former Japanese Prime Minister Okada Keisuke was the commander, he once led ships such as the Nagato and Mutsu to Xiamen for cruising. This visit is the second time. However, the last time there were only more than 30 ships, but this time there are more ships. It is truly an unprecedented event, and it is taking place in the midst of high-profile "Southward Expansion" policies of the Japanese Navy. It can be said to be a major demonstration to Southeast Asia and South China, so its significance is very great.

The 15 destroyers of the Japanese Fifth Torpedo Squadron have been conducting combat exercises on the waters between Xiamen, Taiwan, and Shantou since the 14th of last month, and have not stopped so far. Japanese ships often enter and leave Xiamen Port at night with absolute freedom. In addition, other Japanese ships continue to conduct exercises. In this situation, it is also worth paying attention to. (July 12)

Current Financial Situation in Fujian Province; Si Lie Will Take Office as Director of the Department of Finance; Central Government Subsidies Have Been Finalized 93

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since Xu resigned as Director of the Fujian Provincial Department of Finance in February of this year and Chen Ticheng succeeded him, although he has rigorously reduced staff, reduced salaries, and merged agencies, revenue still cannot meet expenditures. In less than half a year, he has accumulated debts of one million yuan. Chen could not maintain the situation. Recently, the Executive Yuan transferred Chen back to his original post as Director of the Department of Construction, and promoted Si Lie, the Administrative Commissioner of the Fourth District of the province, to Director of the Department of Finance. Si Lie came to the province from Tong'an a few days ago, met Chen Yi to ask for instructions, and then returned to Tong'an to handle the handover. He will not be able to take office in the province until mid-month. It is learned that the reason for Chen Ticheng's departure this time is half because he knew it was difficult and did not want to do it, and half because the Ministry of Finance ordered the abolition of various illegal donations and taxes, but he failed to comply due to financial difficulties, which led to repeated complaints from merchants and dissatisfaction. As for the new Director of the Department of Finance, Si Lie, what confidence does he have in this extremely difficult financial situation (according to Chen Ticheng, the current revenue and expenditure in Fujian province will differ by at least 200,000 yuan per month, no matter what)? Because he has not taken office, it is not yet known. However, Provincial Chairman Chen Yi went to Beijing this time to attend the Second Plenary Session and asked the central authorities to provide relief to the financial situation in Fujian. Yesterday, he sent a telegram to Chen Jinglie, the Secretary-General of the Provincial Government, saying that after entering Beijing, he had visited President Jiang, Minister Kong, and Secretary-General Weng Wenhao to report on the difficult financial situation in Fujian. All the authorities have understood and ordered that a summary of the revenue and expenditure situation in Fujian for the past five years be prepared and sent to Beijing within three days so that a relief plan can be discussed and decided.

The central government subsidies for the province in 1936 have been determined to be 2,656,556 yuan, divided into regular subsidies and temporary subsidies. The regular subsidies include 600,000 yuan for local subsidies, 1,440,000 yuan for education subsidies, and 116,556 yuan for judicial subsidies. The temporary subsidies include 50,000 yuan for Xiamen University, 30,000 yuan for Jimei School, and 240,000 yuan for security team subsidies. In addition, there are three main types of donations and taxes that the Ministry has ordered to be abolished, but cannot be implemented due to the inconvenience of compensating for them. One is the kerosene business tax, one is the seafood business tax, and one is the housing and land tax. Therefore, the disputes with the people are extremely fierce. In addition, the deed tax was originally set at 6% for sales and 3% for mortgages, and later reduced to 4% for sales and 2% for mortgages. Now, an additional 50% is added to fund the primary schools in each county. The special business tax (divided into tea, wood, paper, bamboo shoots, oil, sugar, seafood, and vermicelli) had previously had its tax rates reduced separately to revitalize local products. Now, a special business tax consolidation office has been established to increase tax revenue. The ordinary business tax was originally handled by each merchant guild who voluntarily paid it, but it was later considered to have abuses, and it was taken back and handled by the county governments or tax bureaus, but there was still no improvement. Now, the tax rates have been revised again, and each merchant guild is allowed to handle it in order to facilitate it. (July 11)

Tong Hang-shi Rectifies the Judiciary of All of Fujian 94

Fuzhou Correspondence: Since Chief Justice Tong Hang-shi of the High Court took office, he has been heavily relied upon by the higher authorities to rectify the judiciary in various places. It is now heard that Tong, in order to continue the rectification and renovation, has now drafted a central work plan for 1936. The main points of the outline are as follows: (1) Cases must be concluded within a time limit and must not be delayed to avoid disputes. (2) Prisons should be rectified, and attention should be paid to education and hygiene. (3) Diligence should be examined, and rewards and punishments should be distinguished. (4) Case files should be reorganized. If the case files in various courts and counties are not in a fixed format, they should all be reorganized within a time limit. Those that can be burned should also be cleaned up, listed, and reported. (5) Before the establishment of local courts in each county, judicial offices should be established first to ensure that the trials have an independent spirit. The selection of judges should be carefully selected in accordance with the rules set by the Ministry. It is found that judicial offices will be established in all 19 first-class counties in Fujian Province on July 1.

Chaozhou Customs Inspects Luggage; Tax Revenue from Scattered Items Has Increased Significantly 95

Shantou Correspondence: In order to facilitate the inspection of returning overseas Chinese, the Chaozhou Customs has specially established a luggage inspection office. All luggage and items carried by passengers arriving in Shantou by boat from other ports must be entered on a luggage declaration form. If they are not entered, it will be considered an intentional evasion of customs duties, and they will be confiscated and punished. No matter what agency or organization, they cannot intercede to take them out. They must be redeemed at the auction price. A notice was issued last month to overseas Chinese organizations, shipping companies, and ship compradores. The luggage inspection office was established on the 1st of this month. All imported passenger luggage must be inspected by the office before being released. Even old and scattered items must be taxed. Up to 80 out of 100 people entering the port must pay tax on the spot. Therefore, since the opening, tax revenue has increased greatly. Each time a ship enters the port, the luggage and items waiting for taxation are piled up like a mountain, and passengers arriving in Shantou cannot avoid waiting for one or two hours.

Songjiang: Xi Song-shi Declared Innocent 96

The case of the murder of the wealthy businessman Xi Wei-kun and his wife in Huayangqiao two years ago caused a sensation throughout the city. It was later discovered that Xi Wei-kun's younger brother, Xi Wei-sheng, and his concubine, Song Xiao-mei, had instigated the murder, and Shen A-he, who carried out the murder, was arrested. The county court sentenced them all to death. The defendants refused to accept the sentence and appealed to the Jiangsu High Court, which upheld the original judgment. They then appealed to the Supreme Court. During the appeal, Xi Wei-sheng died in Suzhou Prison. His concubine, Xi Song-shi, was remanded to the High Court for retrial by the Supreme Court. After the witness Kai-kun was summoned again, the debate was finally concluded the day before yesterday. It is now heard from Suzhou that Xi Song-shi has been declared innocent, but has not yet been released.

Wuxi: Three Silk Factories Down Tools in Succession 97

The female workers of the Zhoushan Wufeng Silk Factory in this county went on strike because the factory suppressed and lowered wages. They repeatedly requested the factory to increase wages, but were not granted. On the afternoon of the 12th, a portion of the female workers again requested the factory to increase wages. Because there was no result, it caused a complete strike. At that time, the workers of the nearby Ruichang Silk Factory, hearing of the previous situation, responded by going on strike together. On the one hand, they negotiated with the factory to no avail, and the stalemate could not be resolved. At the same time, the female workers of the Yongsheng Silk Factory at Xiaofenqiao outside the East Gate continued to provide assistance and stopped working together. The factory, seeing that the situation was serious and fearing accidents, closed the factory doors and prohibited entry and exit. On the one hand, it telegraphed the Public Security Bureau to request them to send troops to suppress the situation. The female workers of the Yongsheng Silk Factory, who had been deeply oppressed, took the opportunity to escape and requested assistance from the Silk Industry Workers' Union. The union sent personnel to various factories to mediate until 5 p.m., but the situation had not yet been calmed down.

Continued Land Registration 98

The Land Administration Bureau of this county has recently expanded its bureau affairs and is continuing to handle land registration in the fourth, fifth, sixth, and seventh districts, which will be implemented from the 15th of this month. A total of 65 townships have established 16 registration offices, each with a director in charge. The candidates for director have already been appointed separately.

Danyang: Shop Assistant Robbed While Collecting Debts 99

Liu J眉, a shop assistant from Taihe East in Xianqiao, within the city, a native of Shaoxing, Zhejiang, went to Baozhen Township in Zhenjiang County to collect debts during the old Dragon Boat Festival. However, after he left, there was no news of him. The shop became very worried and telegraphed Baozhen for inquiries. The reply stated that he had left for many days. The shop was greatly alarmed and sent a letter to his family in Danyang, asking people everywhere to inquire. Now it is known that Liu was robbed by bandits on his way back to Danyang after collecting debts in Baozhen and taken to Wuxi. He recently escaped from the bandits' den and has already telegraphed the news.

Regarding the Central River, which concerns both Zhenjiang and Danyang counties, villagers from Toutou Lake Village forcibly built a dam to intercept the flow of the river, obstructing the water conservancy of Huangling and other townships in this county. Disputes have arisen between the two sides, which have been prolonged for a long time without a resolution. Now, Zhu Changfa, the head of Huangling Township, continues to strive for resolution with the provincial authorities. The Construction Department has issued a resolution plan. Discovery of Pseudo-Cholera 102

Jiaxing has had hot weather for several consecutive days, with thermometers exceeding 90 degrees. All agencies and organizations have stopped working in the afternoon. There have been several cases of heatstroke among laborers every day. Charitable organizations are holding clinics to benefit the poor and sick. There have also been discoveries of pseudo-cholera, but fortunately, it is not severe, so it heals after treatment.

Nantong: Zhejiang Warship Trespasses and Causes Trouble 103

The Guangyu No. 2 fishing boat of Shanghai Tongyuan Company was fishing in Chongming Jiushan when the soldiers of the Zhejiang Marine Police Tai'an warship injured the captain, Shi Youxiang, and the first mate, Gu Wendiao. Commissioner Ge of the Nantong District happened to be in Chongming. Upon receiving the report, he immediately handed it over to Gu Hongxi, the head of Chongming County, for verification. Commissioner Wan presented a report to the provincial government on the 11th, stating that the Zhejiang Marine Police Tai'an warship had trespassed and injured fishermen under false pretenses, which was illegal and greatly affected the fishing industry in the district. It is proposed that the provincial government be requested to consult the Zhejiang Provincial Government for strict investigation and handling in order to maintain the fishing industry on the island.

Grain Storage Collection Measures 104

All districts and townships in Tongyi County will establish grain storage warehouses from this month. The city warehouse will store rice, while district and township warehouses can substitute with wheat. The collection of stored grain will be split half and half between landlords and tenants, with three catties collected per mu. 70% will go to the township warehouse, and 30% will go to the district warehouse. Of the amount due to the district warehouse, 70% will go to the district warehouse and 30% to the county warehouse. Regardless of landlords or tenants, those with less than eight mu of land are exempt from collection.

Yangzhou: Bureau Orders Counties to Prevent Flood Season 105

The Jiangdu County Government, due to the order from the Canal Works Bureau to promulgate the provisional measures for flood prevention in various counties along the canal, stated that preparations should be made before the arrival of the flood season and ordered the reporting of compliance. It specially forwarded orders to the heads of the seven districts under the jurisdiction of the county's flood prevention area, stating that the starting and ending points of flood prevention in each county are from Liuzha to Lujin, totaling 16 kilometers in length. In addition to 20 dike-guarding civilians per kilometer, 3,000 temporary rescue civilians are required. Orders were issued to immediately prepare and organize, and to submit a list of dike-guarding and rescue civilians for transfer to the bureau. At the same time, orders were issued to the first to fourth-class district offices to assist in handling the matter at any time.

Gaoyou: Dissolution of the Warehouse Workers' Union 106

The Grain Upper and Lower Warehouse Workers' Union in this county has experienced repeated disputes due to the issue of new and old factions. On June 29th, another dispute arose, and all wheat shops stopped receiving wheat uniformly, resulting in a one-day strike in the entire grain trade, which has not yet been resolved. The county government, after thoroughly investigating the internal organization and external activities of the union since its establishment, found that it had violated items one and three of Article 37 of the Labor Union Law and should be dissolved according to law. In addition to reporting to the Construction Department for record, the county party department was also informed for investigation. Furthermore, the county chamber of commerce was ordered to inform various companies and transport companies that they should not refuse to employ current workers who had participated in the union without reason.

Hangzhou: Relief for Coastal Fisheries 107

Zhejiang Province is a region reliant on salt. The coastal fishermen in Ningbo, Haimen, Yongjia, and other places number in the hundreds of thousands. In recent years, due to low fish prices and the cessation of loans from money shops, fishermen lack funds for fishing, and their livelihoods are in a state of panic. The provincial government has specially established a Fisheries Management Committee to plan relief efforts. It plans to borrow 2 million yuan from the Agricultural Bank of China this autumn fishing season and lend it to fishermen as fishing capital. It is currently actively underway. The government is also guiding fishermen to jointly organize cooperatives with fish shops and ice-fresh boats to jointly handle production and marketing matters.

Holding a General Business Registration 108

The Construction Department is currently planning to conduct a general registration of all companies and businesses in the province. Those who do not comply with the registration regulations will not be allowed to operate and will be forcibly enforced. The months of July and August are designated as the preparation period. The general registration will begin on September 1st and will last for four months, ending at the end of this year. If there are special circumstances in each county, an extension of one month may be granted, but it must be completed by the end of January next year.

Ningbo: Wuling Park to be Completed Soon 109

The Wuling Park in Xikou, Fenghua, has been under active construction since Chairman Chiang ordered its construction. In just over a year, it is now known that the park's construction has been gradually completed. Pavilions, towers, and pavilions compete in beauty, with flowers and trees vying for splendor. Small river boats and green shade cover the sky. It is truly a summer resort. Once the gate in front of the park is completed, it will be completed soon.

Construction of a Contagious Disease Hospital 110

The Yin County Government, considering that there was no contagious disease hospital in the port, initiated preparations and hired gentry and merchants Wang Wenhan and Zhou Dalie as preparation committee members. After several designs, it was decided to build near the You Sheng Guan in the North Gate. In addition to allocating the city base for the hospital base, You Sheng Guan donated three mu of land, and the Yongbei Catholic Church donated one and a half mu. Construction has already begun on the 9th and is expected to be completed within six months.

Cocoon Business Tax: Ministry of Finance Has Agreed to Reduce, Still Charging 2/1000 as in the 20th Year. Zhejiang Cocoon Federation Presented to the Ministry of Finance for Compliance 115

The Zhejiang Cocoon Industry Association Federation, located in Lianzhuli, Avenue Edward VII, Shanghai, presented a document to the Ministry of Finance yesterday, stating: "Regarding the matter of reporting, it was approved by the ministry that the association's presentation on the sudden increase of the cocoon industry business tax to 5/1000, which is illegal, and requested a prompt telegram to Zhejiang to correct it. The approval was received that the presentation had been noted, and the Zhejiang Finance Department was ordered to investigate and handle it." On the 11th of this month, Zhejiang News was read, and the Ministry's instructions to the Zhejiang Finance Department stated: "Silk cocoons have always been a major product of Zhejiang Province. In recent years, foreign sales have been sluggish, and the cocoon industry has declined sharply. In the 21st year, in order to rescue the silk industry, the Zhejiang Provincial Government stipulated that the business tax rate for the industry should still be charged at 2/1000 as in the 20th year. Although the silk cocoon market has slightly improved in recent years, the decline in rural areas and the recovery of vitality are also real. Moreover, the silk cocoon business is of great importance to our international trade. The association's presentation, citing the principles of reducing and exempting business tax and the provisions of Article 4 of the measures, is not without reason. The government should promote and maintain it to alleviate commercial difficulties and benefit foreign sales. In accordance with the aforementioned circumstances, in addition to the instructions, the original presentation should be copied and sent to the department, ordering the department to refer to the established cases over the years and still charge 2/1000. Please inform them accordingly." It is evident that the ministry sympathizes with commercial difficulties and deeply feels the difficulty of exporting raw silk in recent years. The inability to compete in overseas sales is due to the excessive taxes and expenses in China, which prevent costs from being reduced. Now that Zhejiang Province has been approved to refer to the established cases over the years and still charge 2/1000 for the cocoon business tax, in this time of national financial difficulty, both sides should consider and take care of each other. All our merchants should sincerely repay, strive to donate, and mutually maintain the critical situation. In addition to notifying the cocoon industry associations by the association to inform all cocoon merchants to strictly abide by the order and collect the business tax according to 2/1000, and submit it to the respective business tax bureaus for receipt. Before the order, the reason for the cocoon industry to comply with the order and pay taxes is to submit a document to the ministry for review and implementation, which is for public convenience. Sincerely, Finance Minister Kong."

Customs Compiled Import Goods Marking Regulations: The Purpose of These Regulations is to Enable Each Item of Goods to be Identified Solely by its Mark and Number 117

The New News Agency said that Bageisen, the Commissioner of the Jianghai Customs, issued a notice No. 1527, specially compiling the regulations on marking marks and numbers for imported goods from overseas. The notice states that the measures for detailed marking of marks and numbers on the packaging of imported goods from overseas have been issued by the Customs in Notice No. 1242 on September 28, 1932, and Notice No. 1257 on November 16 of the same year. Now, because merchants often have questions about this matter and send letters requesting explanations, the current measures have been compiled into regulations as follows: (1) The purpose of these regulations is to enable each customs to easily identify each item of goods solely by its mark and number. (2) (A) All imported goods must have a mark. This mark should be a clear graphic, such as △, or at least three English letters in a group, such as KCA, or a mark formed by a combination of graphics and English letters, such as △KCA. This mark should be marked on the packaging of the goods in a non-erasable manner, either by printing, stamping, or branding. If there is no packaging, one of the above methods should be selected to mark the goods for identification. (B) For goods packed in boxes, barrels, baskets, cylindrical tubes, etc., if each item does not have a unique number that does not repeat for at least two years, then a non-repeating number or date must be added to the mark. This number can be the starting number of the batch of goods, the order number, or the date of shipment without using a number, such as △8432 △ima No 281 △1636. Other goods packed in bags or packages must have a non-repeating number or date mark or add a different mark composed of at least three English letters in a non-erasable manner. (3) In addition to marking the mark according to the measures in Article 2, each batch of imported goods must also add sequential numbers to each item, such as 10111213, etc. However, for large batches of goods, except for those packed in boxes and barrels, if each item is of the same type and weight, this sequential number does not necessarily need to be added. (4) All the following imported goods do not need to be handled in accordance with the general measures in Articles (2) and (3) above. (A) Non-boxed goods can be marked according to the following measures: angle iron, iron bars, iron bar heads, iron beams, etc. should be marked with green, white, or red paint at both ends; hoop iron should be marked with paint or tied with metal labels; steel sheets and steel plates should be marked with paint according to the measures in Article 2; various tanned hides should be printed with marks according to the measures in Article 2; pipes should be tied with linen or metal labels; various rolled ropes, linen or canvas or metal labels, wood sections should be marked with marks or numbers branded or painted on each section; iron wire and iron wire sections should be tied with metal labels; for other goods, if their nature or packaging makes it impossible to mark in a non-erasable manner according to the measures in Article 2, they should be tied with linen, canvas, or metal strips stating the appropriate mark. (B) Tinplate and other items that are exclusively for the use of importers and their agents or factories and do not need to be re-exported to other trading ports do not need to be marked with numbers again if the marks are already sufficiently clear. (C) Fresh fish, fruits, or vegetables imported do not necessarily need to be marked with numbers or have different shipping numbers marked in accordance with the provisions of Article 2 (B) above. However, these unmarked fresh goods will not be eligible for re-export benefits. (5) If goods are not marked in accordance with the measures in the above articles, they should be re-marked under the supervision of the customs. Every four hours or less than four hours, a fee of 16 yuan in national currency must be paid as usual. If two or more batches of goods, whether transported by the same ship or not, are stored in the same warehouse, and it is found that their marks and numbers are the same or substantially the same, even if they are not transported from one port and are not reported by one declarant or consignee, they must also be re-marked. Therefore, for their own benefit, merchants should pay attention to whether the marks and numbers of all goods are clear. Although the provisions of Article 2 (B) have not been fully complied with by merchants, if they are not complied with after the scheduled implementation of these regulations, they should be re-marked under the supervision of the customs and pay the fees as required. (6) If all items in a batch of goods are of the same type and weight, but only a part of them are declared, the declaration form does not need to state the number of each item, but only state that the declared goods are part of which batch, for example, 10 of 100 items in a batch of goods, that is, state (Io Packages exIot I Ioo). The above six articles are scheduled to be strictly implemented from October 12 of this year. All importing merchants should be informed accordingly. This notice is hereby issued.

This Year's Rice Grain is Expected to Have a Good Harvest: The River Rice is Gradually Dropping in Price, and the New Newly Milled Rice Will be Available in a Month. Various Provinces Have Decided to Build Grain Storage Warehouses 120

The East China News Agency said that from the sowing period to the present, rice field cultivation, thanks to the government's instructions and the farmers' efforts to improve, can be expected to have a good harvest. At the same time, those who study celestial phenomena and climate speculate that there will be no severe drought this year, and the new newly milled rice can be seen in another month. Therefore, the rice price has been very stable recently, unlike the crazy rise last year, which has benefited farmers a lot.

Bumper Harvest of Wheat and Beans, Stable Rice Prices

This year, wheat, barley, and broad beans have all reported bumper harvests. In previous years, due to the poor harvest of wheat and beans, every time the green and yellow seasons overlapped, the hoarding of rice merchants and the accumulation of households would be higher than during the autumn harvest. Last year, it even rose to one-third, which was extremely harmful to farmers who worked hard all year round. Because they had to pay rent and debts after the autumn harvest, they would sell what they had harvested at a low price. By the summer, they had to rely on buying at a high price. Rice merchants and hoarding households took the opportunity to release air and raise rice prices during this period. This year, due to the bumper harvest of wheat and beans, there is no opportunity to take advantage of.

Proper Cultivation Methods, Rice Can Have a Good Harvest

This year's rice, in the provinces dredging rivers, improving technology, guiding cultivation, and removing weeds and pests, with efforts, farmers are not entirely sticking to old methods. They have reformed the technology. The early rice seedlings have been transplanted for more than three months, and the late rice has also been in place for a month. The development and growth are quite smooth, and the fields are green and lovely. Locusts and borers have also been eradicated at any time. According to research, there will be no severe drought this year, so the prospects for rice harvest are very promising.

Low Price of Old Rice, Large Accumulation

Currently, all rice and grain transactions on the market are very smooth, and prices are extremely stable. The reason for this, in addition to the above, is also because the landlords and wealthy gentry in Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Hubei, and Hunan provinces have accumulated a lot of grain. According to estimates from the rice and grain industry, the gentry in the interior have accumulated grain for more than three years without ever selling it. Moreover, the first batch of new rice this year can be released in just one month.

Provincial and County Warehouses Are Being Built One After Another

Currently, the provinces' agricultural warehouses are roughly divided into provincial warehouses, county warehouses, and township warehouses. Each county has two or four or five warehouses to accumulate rice, agricultural tools, agricultural fertilizers, etc. After the autumn harvest this year, the five southeastern provinces will have the latest type of warehouses.

Unified Authority over Grain Management

Regarding the unification of grain management, the Ministries of Finance and Industry have been planning for many years, but there are still no concrete measures. It is learned that there are currently two more or less close proposals: (1) The Grain Transportation and Marketing Bureau continues to operate; (2) Another Grain Transportation and Marketing Committee is formed. The difficulty lies in whether this organization belongs to the Ministry of Industry or the Ministry of Finance, or whether the two ministries jointly form a unit. After this issue is resolved, the authority over management can be unified. However, it is heard that, in any case, it can be resolved during the autumn harvest this year.

Jiangzhe and Zhonghui Banks Discussed Merger and Operation Under the Name of Zhonghui Bank, Effective November 2nd This Year 121

According to Shen Shi News Agency, Jiangzhe Bank, organized by prominent Shanghai merchants, has been thriving since its establishment in the 20th year of the Republic of China. Last year, it even built a new building on Jiangxi Road, establishing a strong reputation. Recently, recognizing that all undertakings must unite to enhance strength and expand business, a merger was proposed. Coincidentally, Zhonghui Bank has been established for many years, with highly developed business credit and comparable assets and operations. Furthermore, there have been close personnel connections, with several individuals serving as directors and supervisors of both banks. All supported the proposal, and yesterday afternoon, extraordinary shareholders' meetings were convened separately to present the merger proposal. Shareholders of both banks unanimously approved the plan, setting November 2nd of this year as the effective date of the merger. According to the law, a three-month public notice period is required. Bank mergers are common in foreign countries, but rare in China. Now, the merger of Jiangzhe Bank and Zhonghui Bank, two major banks, is a good sign for China's financial industry, pioneering bank mergers. In the future, others will likely follow suit. It is also noted that Zhonghui Bank has a paid-up capital of 2 million yuan, while Jiangzhe Bank has a paid-up capital of 1.5 million yuan. Both banks have public reserve funds of 1 million yuan. After the merger, the capital will become 3.5 million yuan, and the business will surely develop further. The name will remain Zhonghui Bank, and all assets and liabilities of Jiangzhe Bank will be assumed by Zhonghui Bank.

Xin Zha Silk Factory Continues Strike, Party and Government Determined to Resolve with Compromise 122

According to Da Gong News Agency, thirteen silk reeling factories in the Xin Zha District, including Dafeng, Chengfeng, Hongtai, Xiexing, Yichang, Tailun, Fuchang, Dongxiang, Dacheng, Meifeng, Fuchang No. 2 Factory, Jiyu, and Jiuyu, employing both male and female silk reeling workers, demanded the restoration of the original wage of 5 jiao and 1 fen per worker. However, due to the factories' financial difficulties and lack of business improvement, this demand was not accepted. Therefore, starting on July 8th, workers from each factory left their jobs and went on strike, which has lasted for five days as of yesterday. The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau convened both parties on the afternoon of July 9th for mediation, but the conditions of the two parties differed greatly, and no results were achieved. The workers of each factory, due to their unfulfilled demands, decided to continue the strike to fight for the final victory.

Party and Government Advice

After the party and government organs jointly convened both parties for mediation without success, deeply concerned that the unrest would expand and affect the factory's business, or that unrest would occur among workers in other districts, they specially dispatched cadres on the afternoon before yesterday, together with the directors and supervisors of the Shanghai Sixth District Silk Reeling Industry Association, to inform the workers' representatives and small team leaders, giving them earnest advice. However, the workers still insisted on restoring the original wage and refused to accept the unconditional return to work, their attitude being very firm.

Further Mediation

The party and government standing committee are extremely concerned about the silk factory worker unrest in Xin Zha District. A compromise solution has now been agreed upon regarding the wage portion. It is scheduled to be presented at the second mediation meeting between labor and management on July 14th to seek opinions from both parties. This solution takes into account both the factory's business burden and the workers' livelihood difficulties. If either party disagrees at that time, no further mediation will be convened, and a written order will be directly issued to both parties to be implemented in accordance with it.

China Foreign Famine Relief Committee Inspects Disaster Report of Juye and Other Counties 123

The China Foreign Famine Relief Committee at 505 Henan Road previously sent Yang Yiming of the Agricultural and Water Conservancy Division to Shandong to inspect the disaster situation in various counties in order to facilitate disaster relief. The following is an excerpt from his report on the disaster situation in Juye and other counties. In Juye, the disaster-stricken area accounts for 60% of the county. Yellow River water flowing from Yuncheng caused severe damage, with the most severely affected villages being located in the northern part of the county. Except for low-lying areas such as Xue Wenji, which were unable to plant autumn crops, the remaining areas are in good condition. Insect infestations previously occurred in the autumn crops, but have now been slightly reduced, but not completely eradicated, which is still concerning. According to County Magistrate Xue Heling, the county received 200,000 yuan in disaster relief funds from various sources, including 25,000 yuan from the Yellow River Commission for city wall repair. The city wall repair work is currently underway, employing over 2,000 workers. Jiaxiang is also a heavily affected area. The Phoenix Mountain and other mountains in the county have a total of 99 peaks. The winding roads made it difficult for the Yellow River water to be discharged, resulting in a submersion lasting for seven months. The county has many high mountains and agricultural crops are not as abundant as in neighboring counties. Furthermore, the area is small and the economy is usually difficult. Since the disaster, it has been even more difficult to save itself, resulting in a barren landscape with no autumn crops planted in areas such as Niuguantun in the west and Lizhuang in the south. The scene is extremely tragic. Statistics show that the disaster area in the county accounts for 94% of the total area. There was no harvest in the wheat season this year, and only half of the autumn crops were planted. Food can only support the people until the end of the year at most, and the spring famine next year is expected. According to County Magistrate Tong Jinbiao, the county is a third-class county and is often overlooked by the outside world. Disaster relief funds received from various sources are less than 40,000 yuan, and he hopes for more relief to save lives. In the Guyuting Village and Nanyang Town area of Yutai, there was no harvest of wheat and autumn crops were rarely planted. Ruined walls and broken tiles are a sad sight, and the disaster situation is more severe than in other counties, due to the low-lying terrain and convergence of rivers. County Magistrate Yang Qidong stated that the disaster area is nearly 95% of the county, and only 60,000 yuan in disaster relief funds has been received, urgently requiring strong assistance from the outside world.

Shanghai-Bound River Rice Found to Be Hot, Reason Being Mechanically Milled Rice Contains Moisture, Rice Market Transactions Stagnant and Prices Trending Downstream 124

According to Da Gong News Agency, recently, due to the hot weather, it happens to be the busy farming season in various villages. Only twenty or so boats of river rice from the northern and southern markets arrive each day. Furthermore, the autumn harvest of grains in various production areas last year were all mechanically milled, containing moisture. During this time of extreme heat, the color easily turns black and hot. Therefore, inland merchants and boat merchants have reduced shipments, and guest merchants dare not purchase and hoard too much, fearing unexpected economic losses. Therefore, the rice market has been very quiet for days, and prices continue to trend downstream. The prices of first and second grade thin rice and broken rice have fallen by one or two jiao per dan. The future of the rice market depends on the weather turning cooler in autumn before improvement can be seen.

When reporters asked various detectives and police officers about the discovery of the handgun, they all refused to discuss it. (Omission) Yesterday afternoon, Mr. Kayo Sei's body was examined at the Feilun Road Examination Office, and a bullet was found, entering from the root of the right ear and remaining in the frontal bone. It is believed that the murderer fired at a very close distance, about three or four feet away. Next to the scene of the incident on Qimei Road is a high cement wall, so some people believe that the murderer may have hidden on the wall, but this is unlikely because the bullet entered from the root of the ear and went up to the forehead. Only one thing can be hinted, that is, the murderer must have been passing by Kayo Sei at the time. The Public Concession Police Station refuses to discuss any possible motives for this case. (Omission) Everything in Hongkou and Zhabei is as peaceful as usual. A small number of Japanese patrols were still patrolling yesterday afternoon, mostly on motorcycles. Japanese marines were stationed at the intersections of the incident.

They immediately hired two yellow rickshaws with British Concession license plates to take them to Fumin Hospital on North Sichuan Road for treatment. Fresh Pork Vendor Association Telegraphed Appeal to the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee to Abolish the Pig Tax Checkpoints in Five Counties of Jiangsu Province 128

Chen Guo, a special commissioner for the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province, and others, in violation of laws and regulations, openly set up checkpoints along the way, extorting money from ships. Pig merchants in various counties could not bear the burden and repeatedly telegraphed the authorities for thorough investigation. Explicit orders were also issued to correct the situation. However, Chen Guo and others not only failed to reform but intensified their actions, setting up checkpoints at every turn, with as many as twenty locations. Pig merchants in various counties, unable to endure any longer, jointly telegraphed the Shanghai Fresh Pork Vendor Association, requesting them to appeal on their behalf. The following is a transcript of the association's telegram to the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee: "To all members of the Central Executive Committee, we humbly submit a joint telegram from Xu Liu, a merchant from Nantong County, Jiangsu Province, Cong Yixing, a pig merchant from Rugao County, Zhang Yiyuan, a pig merchant from Dongtai County, and twenty-six others, stating that Chen Guo, the special commissioner for the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province, and others, stubbornly resist laws and regulations, privately set up checkpoints, and harshly extort and collect taxes. They earnestly request that the situation be reported and a thorough investigation be conducted, strictly abolishing the original checkpoints as soon as possible to uphold the law and protect the people's livelihood. It has been found that Chen Guo, in collusion with Tang, bid on and contracted with the finance department to handle the business tax on the transportation of pigs in five counties in northern Jiangsu Province. Ignoring their avarice, they set up numerous tax checkpoints, exploiting merchants' wealth. The Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce has repeatedly appealed to the provincial government, ordering them to comply with the ministry's order, handle the matter according to the established practice of payment by the trade. On May 14th of this year, the Ministry of Finance issued telegram No. 4152, stating that it had previously received telegrams requesting that the Jiangsu Provincial Government be consulted to order the department to maintain the established practice of payment by the pig trade and to explicitly eliminate the illegal and excessive taxation by contractors. The Jiangsu Provincial Government had been consulted accordingly, and the Ministry's repeated consultations had been forwarded for compliance. The Jiangsu Provincial Government's document No. 105, dated April 28th of this year, stated that the case had been previously reported to the province by the Shanghai General Chamber of Commerce, and the special commissioner for the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province had been repeatedly instructed to handle the matter carefully in accordance with regulations and not to set up checkpoints for extortion, causing harassment. The previous reasons were approved, and it was further instructed to comply with regulations. This was duly consulted and replied. It was approved that a telegram should be sent to inform, etc., and duly delivered to the association. Upon receiving this, the merchants celebrated, hoping that the tribulation of taxes would be removed and that there would be a chance for recovery. Unexpectedly, for a month, Chen Guo and Tang refused to comply and continued to illegally collect taxes and extort as before. The provincial government's clear orders were treated as mere formalities. Their arrogance and stubborn resistance were beyond words. Historically, pig tax has been collected at various ports along the river when pigs are exported and sold. There has never been the harm of inland checkpoint taxation. In October of the 21st year of the Republic of China, the Rugao Business Tax Bureau, with a whimsical idea, privately established tax checkpoints in Dingyan, Matang, Baipu, and other places in the interior to collect pig tax. Merchants publicly elected representatives to petition in Beijing and the province. The provincial department explicitly ordered the immediate abolition of the checkpoints and changed the pig tax to the business tax on the transportation of pigs in five counties in northern Jiangsu Province, entrusting Special Commissioner Lou Fumin to manage it and imitating the original port collection in northern Jiangsu. On November 26th of that year, the special commissioner received an explicit order from the provincial department to abolish the tax checkpoints in Matang, Baipu, etc. In May of the 23rd year, after Chen Guo contracted, he dared to reinstate the Dingyan, Matang, and Baipu checkpoints that had been explicitly abolished and added tax checkpoints in Liqiao, Maqiao, and other places that had not been subject to checkpoints for hundreds of years, repeatedly blocking and harshly extorting transit taxes. Dozens of businesses have been bankrupted by their power. Among the five counties in northern Jiangsu, only Tongzhou has a special situation. All pigs coming to Tongzhou must pass through Dingyan, Matang, Baipu, Liqiao, Maqiao, and other places. The tax cannot be unified and collected according to the established practice of payment by the trade, so that the same tax has different routes. Moreover, when pig boats arrive at the checkpoints, they are deliberately delayed. The checkpoint staff may not be up early, or they may be out late. There are also times for eating, resting, entertaining, caulking the hold, counting, and issuing tickets. If the tax checkpoint is short even a small amount, the merchants are forced to travel dozens of miles to borrow money to make up the difference. Pigs are fresh goods. Once they are blocked and delayed, they are easily injured or die, which is a significant matter. In the past, when taxes were paid by the trade, the trade would advance all payments, avoiding all kinds of difficulties along the way. Since the implementation of checkpoint taxation and extortion, not only has the trade stopped, but laborers who rely on pigs to maintain their families, such as sand boat workers on the Yangtze River, barge workers on inland rivers, and cart drivers who push pigs, number over ten thousand. The impact will lead to starvation. Blocking pig boats coming to Tongzhou on the main waterways and extorting taxes has gradually cut off our livelihoods. There are no checkpoints on the rivers of Rugao, Taixing, Jiangdu, and Jingjiang. Why do they exclusively antagonize Tongzhou, abuse our pig merchants, and trample on our lifelines? The unequal treatment is intolerable in law and reason. Moreover, Chen Guo, in collusion with Tang, has colluded with corrupt officials and owes more than 30,000 yuan in contracted tax payments, using this as a means to seek renewal of the contract. The annual pig tax is over 180,000 yuan, deceiving those above and below, with insatiable desires. They even further increased the tax rate, pests that harm the people, worse than snakes and scorpions. If you do not believe it, please send personnel to investigate the number of pigs sold daily by the Shanghai Fresh Pork Trade Association from May 21st of the 22nd year to May 21st of the 24th year and verify the allocation of expenses for river protection vessels from each trade. There is no error. The merchants felt a chill upon hearing the wicked names of these people. When they contracted the pig tax in Tongzhou, they all cried out in pain and hatred. From then on, the lives of our families were entirely in the hands of these poisonous people. Like mercury falling to the ground, they infiltrated everywhere, and now everything has become a reality, clearly verifiable. Such coercion and violation of the law undermine the credibility of national policies. The merchants have suffered abuse and hardship, finding themselves in a situation of nine deaths and no life, in a place where they can no longer endure. They have no choice but to cry out and appeal for relief. In addition to enclosing a map of the port and river tax checkpoints and a copy of the former Special Commissioner Lou's original order abolishing the Dingyan, etc., tax checkpoints, we urgently request your association to investigate and relay the appeal, strictly ordering the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province to comply with provincial orders as soon as possible, abolishing all illegal tax checkpoints in Dingyan, Matang, Baipu, Liqiao, Maqiao, etc., and dismissing and prosecuting Chen Guo and Tang, appointing virtuous officials to take over, to relieve public anger and uphold the law. This is indeed a matter of public justice. It is approved that Chen Guo, the special commissioner for the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province, and others, illegally collect taxes and privately set up checkpoints along the way, extorting money from ships. This association has repeatedly received letters from pig merchants in various counties requesting us to appeal on their behalf. We have relayed their appeals to the Ministry of Finance and the Jiangsu Provincial Government for thorough investigation. Subsequently, we received instructions to comply with the legal tax rate and not to impose excessive taxes. However, the business tax on pigs in northern Jiangsu has not only not been corrected, but checkpoints are still set up to intercept ships and collect taxes as before. Moreover, the practice has intensified, with checkpoints set up at every turn, with as many as twenty locations (see attached map). This is truly appalling. Article 3 of the Business Tax Law states that all businesses subject to business tax should provide the following information and apply for a business tax investigation certificate: item 1 specifies the type of business, store name, and location. However, very few pig merchants have stores. The source of pigs is mostly small purchases from farmers or wholesale purchases from pig traders, which are then transported to various ports for sale. To collect taxes from those who have not set up stores contradicts the Business Tax Law, which stipulates that taxation only occurs where stores are opened. Furthermore, Article 7 of the same law states that business tax may be collected annually, semi-annually, or quarterly, depending on the circumstances considered by the provincial and municipal governments. However, short-term business taxes may be collected monthly in accordance with the provisions of Articles 3 to 6. Even if pig merchants have an obligation to pay business tax, it should be collected annually or quarterly. If it is considered short-term in nature, it can be changed from quarterly to monthly. There are no other changes to the collection method. However, the business tax collection office for pigs in northern Jiangsu Province arbitrarily sets up checkpoints along the way, intercepting ships and collecting taxes daily. This contradicts the Business Tax Law. Furthermore, the fourth of the five items in the national financial conference proposal for reorganizing business tax clearly stipulates that business tax should not be collected on goods, and the principle of collecting tax on employment should be applied. The practice of collecting business tax similar to transit fees on goods should be abolished. The original methods of merchant associations assisting in collection, contracting, and apportioning among industries should be reformed by local authorities. The fifth item in the plan for reorganizing local finances stipulates that taxes that obstruct traffic or are levied on goods or boats passing through should not be collected. This is the third contradiction. Now, the collecting commissioner not only violates business tax laws and regulations but also acts arbitrarily, setting up checkpoints to intercept ships and collecting multiple taxes on the same item, which is particularly illegal. Since the nationwide abolition of transit fees was announced, except for those with specified tax rates to compensate, no taxes may be levied on goods within the same territory. This is explicitly prohibited by Article 612 of the Code. However, within the same jurisdiction of Jiangsu Province, checkpoints are set up at every turn to intercept ships and extort multiple taxes on the same item. This illegal and chaotic government is deeply shocking. The original cause is the undesirable system of reporting, bidding, and contracting by businesses. Those who bid seek to be selected, competing with high prices. The higher the price, the more severe the exploitation of merchants. Once selected, they disregard laws and regulations and do not understand the overall situation, only knowing to maximize profits. Merchants and the people cannot bear the burden, and the pig trade is directly harmed. Farmers are indirectly affected. At a time when all industries are declining and rural areas are bankrupt, maintaining recovery is already precarious. There is no reason for the existence of this undesirable contracting system, private establishment of transit fees, and illegal harassment. Moreover, Jiangsu Province is close to the capital, and government orders cannot be implemented. Remote areas will be even less likely to comply. Now, at the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, wise elders of the party and the nation are gathered, promoting benefits and reforming currencies. All people look forward to this. In order to maintain the lives of millions of pig merchants and farmers, this association dares to submit a map of the tax checkpoints set up along the way in various counties of northern Jiangsu, the Ministry of Finance's instructions, and a copy of the instructions of the former special commissioner for the business tax on the transportation of pigs in northern Jiangsu Province, requesting discussion and instruction to the competent authorities to immediately abolish the tax checkpoints along the way, severely punish illegal officials, to relieve pig merchants from their distress and save the people's livelihood from death. The Shanghai Fresh Pork Vendor Association bows in anticipation of your urgent decision.

Anhui Native Association in Shanghai Petitions: Wuyuan County Should Be Under the Jurisdiction of Anhui 130

The Anhui associations in Shanghai telegraphed the Second Plenary Session of the Central Executive Committee, stating: "In order to continue to petition that Wuyuan be returned to the jurisdiction of Anhui, we implore your review and approval to comply with public opinion." The case of Wuyuan being placed under the jurisdiction of Jiangxi has been met with group petitions by public organizations in Wuyuan and fellow natives in other provinces and counties since the explicit order was issued. The relevant authorities were petitioned to not consider the matter, but the request was not granted. After the takeover, it was argued that the original decision was made by the Central Political Conference and could not be changed without review and relief from the highest authority. Therefore, this association and others successively petitioned the Fifth Plenary Session of the Fourth Central Committee, the Sixth Plenary Session, and the Fifth National Congress, requesting re-examination and transfer to the National Government, requesting that Wuyuan be returned to the jurisdiction of Anhui. The above is a general outline of the case's history. Wuyuan has a long history of belonging to Anhui, and its people, language, customs, lifestyle, and environment are the same as those of the five counties of Huizhou. Whether viewed from a political, livelihood, or cultural perspective, there is no need for the change of jurisdiction. Native associations in various locations have spoken in great detail about this, filling numerous volumes, which shows the will of the people. It is believed that the government's important reason for declaring the change of jurisdiction was to facilitate the suppression of bandits, which was only a temporary measure. Now, several years have passed, and the bandits in the neighboring counties of Jiangxi have been cleared, but Wuyuan is still plagued by bandits and has not been stabilized. It would be better to still be under the jurisdiction of Anhui, together with the other five counties of Huizhou, under the guidance of the Tenth District, to cultivate self-defense and assist the garrison troops. As for other details, previous decisions and documents have been repeatedly stated. Now they are compiled into a volume and attached to the document. We implore your review and approval to return Wuyuan to the jurisdiction of Anhui to comply with public opinion. We are extremely apprehensive and await your decision. Respectfully submitted to the Second Plenary Session of the Central Committee of the Chinese Kuomintang, with one volume of compiled documents attached. Native Associations of Weining in Shanghai, Huining Guildhall in Shanghai, Wuyuan Native Association in Shanghai."
