My Country's Chemical Industry Has Begun to Develop Gradually in Recent Years Progress in Heavy Industry is Very Slow The Alcohol Industry is Still Insufficient to Meet Demand 133

The Shen Shi She reported that according to a leading figure in the industrial sector, the development of China's chemical industry is very recent. Therefore, compared with advanced countries, it is not enough to follow their lead. The chemical industry can be roughly divided into heavy industry, light industry, and the alcohol industry. Chemical heavy industry includes the manufacturing of munitions, pigments, pharmaceuticals, enamel, celluloid, soda water, soap, monosodium glutamate, etc. The most important raw materials required are sulfuric acid and ammonia. The first company in China to manufacture these chemical raw materials was the Pacific Alkali Company in Tianjin. Later, the Jiangnan Shipyard of the Navy also set up a factory to manufacture sulfuric acid. With the establishment of the Tianyuan Electrochemical Plant, the domestically produced raw materials like hydrochloric acid, caustic soda, salt chemicals, and lime began to make important advancements, recovering a considerable amount of leakage. Chemical light industry factories, due to their lighter capital requirements, have been set up in China in countless numbers. The largest chemical alcohol industry is the China Alcohol Factory, a joint venture between the Ministry of Industry and the overseas Chinese Huang Jiangquan. There is also the Meilong Alcohol Factory, which is also well-equipped. However, because China needs more than 225 million kilograms of chemical alcohol annually (according to customs import statistics), the output of the two factories is still insufficient to meet demand. It is reported that the Academia Sinica has now established a specialized research department for the alcohol industry, which may be of great benefit to the general chemical industry in the future.

Ningbo Native Association Sends Letter to Yin County Government Itemizing Methods for Relocating Graves 134

The Ningbo Native Association in Shanghai sent a letter to the Yin County Government yesterday regarding the relocation of graves, and itemized three methods. The following is a transcription: We are writing to you, the Yin County Government, in response to your previous official letter regarding the overall plan for reorganizing graves. We were entrusted with presenting the opinions of our fellow villagers so that they could be adopted as much as possible within the scope of the law when drafting the plan. This demonstrates the Yin County Magistrate's earnest desire to seek the hidden desires of the people. Our association members have repeatedly held meetings and discussions, summarizing the opinions of our fellow villagers and formulating three practical methods. We have prepared another letter and pray that they be adopted in your proposed overall plan. We are deeply grateful. Furthermore, regarding the actual implementation in various towns and townships, there are things that we must ask for special attention. The customs of our Ningbo people place great importance on ancestral graves. The heads of various towns and townships must, while implementing laws and regulations, extremely respect existing customs, so that implementation is beneficial and does not cause disputes. For example, the Yin County Coffin Burial Office has been demolishing and relocating floating coffins for more than ten years, and there has been no local objection at first, because the deadline was relatively generous and the procedures were cautious. The office urges the relocation of floating coffins in stages and phases, marking each grave to be relocated so that the grave owner can know at a glance. Those who voluntarily relocate and request an extension are always granted. This is one point. For graves that are relocated on behalf of the owners, they are numbered and listed when relocated to facilitate identification. Coffins are never opened unless they are so decayed that they cannot be moved, in order to prevent theft of burial objects. This is the second point. Recently, various towns and townships have been handling graves uniformly, setting extremely short deadlines. When people go to register, there is no one in charge. When demolishing and relocating, they rely on earthworkers to profit from their income, calculating prices per grave and focusing on profit. The beginning is not good, and the abuses are growing, causing widespread criticism. If they can be ordered to follow the methods of the burial office, there will be many remedies in practice. Therefore, we have attached one or two suggestions and pray that you will examine and implement them. This is what we hope for. Respectfully submitted to Yin County Magistrate Chen.

Three Suggestions The association's itemized suggestions for reorganizing graves: (1) Various towns and townships must first complete the establishment of public cemeteries and public burial grounds before urging the relocation of floating coffins in the towns and townships and prohibiting the construction of graves on cultivated land. On June 2nd of this year, the Hangzhou Southeast Daily reported on a news item about Hangzhou requesting a ban on private cemeteries, which can be used as a reference. (2) According to provincial orders, whether a long-buried grave should be relocated depends on whether it interferes with hygiene, transportation, or land use. Long-buried graves do not pose a hygiene problem. The relationship between transportation and land use should also have clear standards to be followed. For graves along railways and highways that are deemed to be demolished, the distance standards should be explicitly defined in laws and regulations and announced in advance to avoid making the grave owners feel at a loss. (3) In Yin County's single-handed method of registering graves, it is not clearly stated whether the term "grave" refers specifically to the grave itself or includes the coffin. The method of public announcement is also not clearly defined. Article 3 of the provincial supplementary methods states that even if a deadline is set, the principle is not to relocate on behalf of the owners, and an extension should still be publicly announced. However, the registration method only sets a one-year deadline, and those who do not register after the deadline will be treated as ownerless and relocated to Yishan on their behalf. All should be revised in accordance with the supplementary methods. As for the method of requiring grave owners to fill in the registration number on the corner of the grave after registration, it is also not comprehensive. It should be changed to have the township office mark each grave to be relocated in advance, following the method of the county burial office demolishing and relocating floating coffins. This would be more thorough.

Yellow Sea Cyclone Strikes Shanghai's Heatwave Disappears More Extreme Heat in Two to Three Days

Shanghai's weather has been extremely hot in recent days. However, after the end of the rainy season yesterday (the twelfth), the heat gradually dissipated. Since the morning, cool breezes have blown, slightly dispelling the summer heat. Although the sky was clear, the scorching sun did not wreak havoc. The general public speculated that a hurricane was coming. However, according to the observatory, the northeasterly winds yesterday were caused by a cyclone in the Yellow Sea, which was accompanied by low pressure passing through this area and moving northeast. Therefore, the sky was cloudy all day. No hurricane was found in the Yellow Sea or East China Sea. Based on this observation, it can be avoided that Shanghai is hit by a hurricane. Furthermore, the season is approaching the beginning of the dog days, and there will be more extreme heat in two to three days.

The Tongyi Creditor Group Held a Representative Assembly Yesterday to Organize a Debt Collection Team to Seek Compensation from Directors and Supervisors Tomorrow 137

The creditor group organized by the depositors of Tongyi Trust Company in this city held its second representative assembly yesterday afternoon. It was decided to organize a debt collection team and submit petitions to the Ministry of Finance and the Bureau of Social Affairs, requesting orders for the directors and supervisors of the company to be responsible for repayment. Fifteen directors were elected and it was decided that tomorrow (the 14th), they would seek compensation from the directors and supervisors. Details are as follows:

Creditor Meeting

The company's creditor group held its second general representative assembly at 2:00 PM yesterday at the Tianhou Palace, No. 3 District Party Department, North Henan Road. Over 250 creditors attended, including Liu Zhuangwen, Wu Yingxue, Liu Shirong, He Xijun, Gu Hongsheng, He Pinglong, Chen Guanqun, Zhang Huizhen, Shen Qinqing, Zhang Kelun, Liu Donghai, Xing Minyi, Hu Ying, Ge Limin, Gu Difan, Jiang Shi, Chen Lin, Hong Xiuqing, and Sun Cheng, representing a total debt of over 275,700 yuan. Sun Cheng was elected chairman and Zhu Zhaorui was the recorder.

Resolutions Passed

(1) A proposal to petition the Ministry of Finance and the Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs to order the company's directors and supervisors to be responsible for repayment was discussed and passed. Signed. (2) A formal resolution to organize a debt collection team and elect directors. It was resolved to elect fifteen people as directors: Liu Donghai, Xing Minyi, Zhang Kelun, Hu Ying, Ge Limin, Gu Difan, Jiang Shi, Chen Lin, Hong Xiuqing, Gu Qinzhen, Sun Cheng, Qiu Shigan, Chen Jiahao, Ma Fugao, and Zhu Zhaorui. The powers of the board of directors are to execute the resolutions of the assembly. A quorum of more than half of the members is required to convene a board meeting. A proposal to elect representatives to question the directors and supervisors of the company about repayment methods was discussed and passed. It was resolved that all directors should go to question on behalf of the group. (4) Regarding the reconciliation method of the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, it should be based on the deadline stipulated by the Ministry of Finance, otherwise reconciliation should be rejected. (5) A resolution to organize a debt collection team immediately. It was resolved to hand it over to the board of directors for handling. (6) A proposal on how to raise funds for the group. It was resolved that attendees should first pay one yuan, and the board of directors will set the future amount. (7) A resolution on the date of the next assembly. It was resolved to hold it at 2:00 PM on the 16th.

The Murder Case in Liuzao Town, Nanhui, Transferred to Shanghai for Trial. Ma Shouren's Stolen Boat, Shen Shuiliang Tragically Died. 138

Ma Shouren, the owner of Ma Yilong's store and the richest man in Liuzao Town, Nanhui County, along with Shen Shunkui, a clerk in the town, and Zhou Xinqiao, Wang Wenbiao, and Gu Chuntao, members of the local merchant corps, and Huang Yifu, the chief of the Liuzao police (Huang was not brought to justice), were accused by Shen Lu, the wife of the Shen family in Shenjia House, north of Shenjia Stone Bridge, along with her daughter-in-law Shen Zhou, in the Jiangsu High Court. The accusation was that on December 23rd of last year, at around 3:00 PM, Ma Shouren falsely accused her son, Shen Shuiliang, of theft and caused him to be murdered while being escorted, pushed into the river to hide the traces, and that the original county trial was suspected of being biased. The Jiangsu High Court ruled that the Shanghai District Court would be the first court to accept the case. Yesterday, the Nanhui County Government had already transferred the entire case file to the Shanghai Court Procuratorate for investigation and ordered both parties to submit themselves. The facts of the incident and the reasons relied upon by both parties are recorded as follows. Ma Shouren is the wealthiest man in Liuzao Town. The incident stemmed from the theft of a small boat. On December 23rd of last year, at 3:00 PM, Shen Shuiliang, 26 years old, who had been a carpenter, was arrested by Wang Wenbiao, Zhou Xinqiao, and other members of the local merchant corps. According to the merchant corps' record, Shen Shuiliang had confessed to stealing the boat, but the family of the deceased claimed that he was tortured to confess. On the same day, late at night, Jin Shiying, a cook from the local public security bureau, and Qian Shaolin, Zhou Xinqiao, Wang Wenbiao, and Min Shusheng, members of the merchant corps, pretended to escort him to recover the stolen goods. On the way, they strangled Shen with a rope and threw his body into the river, intending to frame someone else. However, according to the defendants, while going to recover the stolen goods, when Shen Shuiliang reached the Chenjia Bridge, west of Bazao Port Bridge, Shen Shuiliang, fearing punishment, jumped into the river to escape, but because his hands were tied, he drowned and they were unable to rescue him. Later, the public security bureau reported to the general bureau, which forwarded it to the county government. Judge Jiang and the coroner went to examine the body. According to the report, the deceased had three rattan marks near the right side of his back, about an inch long and slightly slanted, slightly blue and swollen. His right arm had two rattan marks, both with broken skin and blood stains. Both wrists had rope marks near the top, and the throat also had rope marks. The coroner's report and autopsy were taken by the family of the deceased and photographed, which they used to file a lawsuit, claiming that the rattan marks on the body proved non-criminal torture, the rope marks on the wrists proved the state of being tied, and the rope marks on the throat were evidence of strangulation. They also claimed that when the body was recovered, the abdomen was not swollen, indicating that he fell into the water after death. On the other hand, the defendants did not admit to the injuries all over the body, and claimed that there was no strangulation. They said that strangulation would require breaking the windpipe. The dispute was brought to the county government, causing a sensation throughout the county. After the incident, Ma Shouren was detained for the New Year, and was later released on bail with 1,000 yuan in cash and 1,000 yuan in written guarantee. Shen Shunkui was released on bail with a 500 yuan shop guarantee, and Zhou Xinqiao and Wang Wenbiao were each released on bail with 300 yuan shop guarantees. The dispute has lasted for seven months and has not been resolved. Both sides insist on the points of dying after falling into the river and falling into the river before dying, which is the focus of the dispute. The public opinion is also not very favorable, so the case was submitted to the Jiangsu High Court to transfer jurisdiction to the Shanghai District Court. Yesterday, the deceased's mother, Lu, and the deceased's wife, Zhou, arrived at the court with a four-year-old orphan. The defendants were Ma Shouren, Shen Shunkui, Zhou Xinqiao, Wang Wenbiao, and Gu Chuntao. Chief Prosecutor Zhong Shangbin transferred the case to Li Xulin, the newly appointed prosecutor, for investigation and instructed him to be cautious. After the preliminary hearing, Ma Shouren was required to provide two additional substantial shop guarantees, and the others were also required to provide security guarantees, pending investigation. It is heard that the investigation procedures are that because the Nanhui autopsy report is quite ambiguous, it is planned to transport the coffin to the Zhenru Forensic Institute for re-examination to determine how he fell into the river and died, in order to handle the case.

The City's Tiger Stoves Have Not Increased Prices, but the Water Prices Among Businesses Are Inconsistent. The Price of Tofu Is Chaotic After the Price Increase. 139

The residents of this city mostly rely on hot water shops (commonly known as tiger stoves) for hot water. Due to the dense population of the city, the number of hot water shops is quite large, no less than several thousand, scattered throughout the streets and alleys. Recently, there were rumors that the industry would raise prices after the increase in tofu prices. Yesterday, according to a reporter from the Datong News Agency, after inquiring from the industry, this was not true. The reason is that the industry does not yet have a trade association organization, and the prices are mostly determined independently. In the concession area, the general price for hot water is two to three scoops per copper coin, while in the city area, it is three to four scoops per copper coin, which is very inconsistent. If prices are to be increased, it is necessary to start with unifying water prices. Since water prices are not yet uniform, price increases are out of the question. It was also learned that after the tofu industry raised prices on June 1, the prices are still chaotic. Not only is there no consistency between the special zone and the city area, but the prices in the South City and Zhabei are also different. The industry association originally had an organization to regulate market prices, but recently, due to difficulties in collecting membership fees, the members have not been attending meetings, so there is no way to rectify the situation.

At around 10:00 PM last night, a man suddenly arrived at the Central Hotel at 545 Guangdong Road, leading a boy of about fifteen or sixteen years old. Unexpectedly, at 10:30 PM, Yang Jixian jumped from the fourth-floor window and committed suicide. He fell to the street, his skull was shattered, and his arms and legs were broken. Later, his son was taken to the police station. It is said that there was also a suicide note, which was also taken away by the police. Yang Jixian died at 11:00 PM due to his serious injuries, despite medical treatment.

A Midsummer Afternoon Trip—Impressions of the Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach 141

Special Article from This Newspaper. A friend who recently came to Shanghai from Peiping said that he once asked a lady who had just returned from playing in Shanghai:

"Now that you've come from Shanghai, can you tell me what Shanghai is really like?"

"Well, Shanghai?" The lady replied with an obvious look of disappointment, "I can't see anything new. I just feel that there are houses everywhere. Outside the houses are roads, and the roads are full of people!"

Indeed, even those who are used to living in Shanghai have this feeling. Every day they open their eyes, their bodies are in the house, and there are already many people in the house who have the same thoughts as themselves. They run from home or the office onto the road, and the streets are full of people, even more than in the house. Repeating this back in the house, they meet people again. Shanghai's land is narrow, the houses are small, and the people are many. This Peiping lady's description is quite adequate.

In the summer, these three aspects of Shanghai—narrow land, small houses, and many people—make people feel particularly fearful, except for the very few privileged class. So, on a certain afternoon when the indoor temperature was as high as ninety-six degrees, I accompanied my friend from Peiping, whom I mentioned at the beginning, to Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach, braving the heat.

We were already on the ferry. The water in the Huangpu River was as turbid as flowing cement. The sun was shining directly at noon, a sun that was motionless and stifling, steaming the river water, and a smell like that from a hot oil pot came out of the rippling waves. We sat in the cabin for a while, and felt the sweat on our backs had gone from damp to dripping. So, we took off our long clothes, held light fans—in fact, the fan in my friend's hand was a palace fan with carvings of imperial poems on the ribs, measuring one foot two or three inches long. We walked out of the cabin, picked two canvas chairs on the deck, and sat facing the bow. A bell rang on the boat, and the ship slowly left the dock. The noisy sounds on the shore gradually faded away, until we could no longer distinguish whether the person sitting on the rickshaw was male or female. The ferry had already sailed towards the center of the river, heading north.

Gusts of river wind, although somewhat like they were blowing out of a kitchen or bathroom, could not resist the continuous blowing, and the sweaty backs and canvas chair backs no longer stuck together. The large fan in my friend's hand had already been folded and held in his hand. He gently tapped his thighs and palms. On such a hot afternoon, he had an attitude of leisure like a "clear wind and bright moon" night. I'm afraid you wouldn't find this kind of person even in a room with air conditioning.

Looking closely, there were a dozen canvas chairs around. Several foreigners were sitting there, pointing at both banks of the river, chatting casually. The wind blew over the head of a Western lady, and strands of golden hair hung down beside her black and round sunglasses. She raised her hand and brushed them to the side, and stretched her neck and shook her head. We looked again at the empty canvas chairs, leaned our heads back, and rested as leisurely as possible.

Many cargo ships from foreign countries were moored in the river. Cranes were lifting bundles of goods, some unloading, some loading. The laborers, stripped to the waist and covered in a shiny layer of sweat, were busy working under the sun. Our ferry passed by the side of the ships, and we heard the rumbling of the steam engines driving the cranes, sometimes near, sometimes far, sometimes continuous, sometimes intermittent. Several cargo ships had already passed by us.

After passing Xidu, Donggou, Qingning Temple... the ferry was busy turning, docking, reversing, and going forward. Suddenly, my friend pointed to a huge white ship rushing forward behind the stern and told me to look at the name of the ship next to the keel. In an instant, the two ships were sailing side by side. The ship looked to be about 20,000 tons, all white, with green near the waterline. The white waves split to the left and right sides of the hull. The steady, confident, and proud figure seemed to be reigning over the Huangpu River, looking around with pride. I looked closely at the bow and knew that the ship was named "Filex Roussel," a French mail ship. My friend had lived in Europe for a long time and was experienced in traveling. He said, "Don't just admire her current stability and leisure on the river. Once she reaches the Indian Ocean, if she encounters bad weather, she will be tossed around like a basket. Moreover, once she reaches the Mediterranean, the stifling heat is far worse than our comfort on this ferry!"

The ship arrived at Gaoqiao, we got on a public bus, and in less than twenty minutes, we arrived at the seaside bathing beach. I was revisiting an old place. I already had a good idea of the general situation there. My friend, however, was visiting for the first time, and he couldn't help but miss things while looking around. He told me afterwards that he had originally thought that this seaside bathing beach would just be a Shanghai slang term for "a showy affair," but he didn't know that there was actually a beach. Although it couldn't compare to the grandeur of Qingdao and Dalian, it was much better than a cement-paved swimming pool. There was also a large dining hall, a small garden, a thatched hall, and yurts, where you could swim, fish, and rest. His final conclusion was, "It's quite impressive!" He undoubtedly revealed his personality in his satisfaction.

We first sat in the thatched hall by the beach for a while, sipping some ice water. The atmosphere of the sea enveloped our whole bodies, and gusts of sea wind continued to attack us. Unable to withstand such internal and external cooperation, a heart full of煩熱, had long since vanished. My friend even rented a swimsuit and really took a proper seawater bath. I ran along the beach for a while, looking at the blue and white striped awnings in the north. Further up the shore, there were dozens of small houses in a row, with green gauze windows, and some miscellaneous trees planted in front. The front faced the sea, and the back was full of fields and vegetable gardens. I thought to myself, seeing this scene under the scorching sun was already quite cool. If I could really stay here for a night or two, lying in the dark night and listening to the sound of the tide in the sea, plus a lot of cool wind, and far away, a few whistles of night航, would I need to cover myself with a thin cotton blanket? Thinking of this, I couldn't help but feel a chill in my heart, so I turned back, walked past the sprinkler of the shower, and saw four young girls of similar stature lined up waiting to be photographed. Their laughter broke my "chill." I thought I'd better go see my friend, so I walked towards the beach, where the wind was really lovely, blowing in from my sleeves and trouser legs, and I suddenly swelled up and became plump. At this moment, I passed the small pavilion that rented out swimming toys, and there were several hollow rubber people hanging there. Their "empty appearance" was somewhat similar to my clothes shell that had been blown up by the wind. Just as I was about to burst out laughing, my friend floated his head on the surface of the water and shouted in a loud voice.

"Hey, old friend, what are you doing there in a daze? Why don't you come down and soak too!"

"That's enough," I replied in a loud voice. "It's not bad here, is it?"

My friend's mouth had just uttered the words "interesting," when a wave rolled in, and he started moving his hands and feet again.

We didn't leave the beach until six o'clock. When we parted, I said to my friend:

"If your friend, a certain lady, decides to come to Shanghai again, why not ask her to take a trip to Gaoqiao?" (EL)

Tourists at Gaoqiao Seaside Bathing Beach

(Photo by Lie)

Suicide by Jumping from Zhongxing Villa—Ma Mingli Suffered a Severe Mental Breakdown, Tired of Life, and Died from Injuries Sustained from Jumping. 142

Ma Mingli, a native of Yuyao, 31 years old, worked at the Bank of China and had a history of mental illness. At 7:30 AM yesterday, he suffered a severe mental breakdown in his dormitory on the fourth floor of Zhongxing Villa, 155 Gsi Fleisher Road, West Shanghai. He suddenly lost his mind, and the thought of being tired of life arose. He jumped from the fourth-floor window, immediately injuring his head, abdomen, and arms severely. He was barely breathing. After someone reported it to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau, the police rushed to the scene and took him to a hospital in West Shanghai for treatment. However, the treatment was ineffective, and he died shortly after. Later, relatives and friends went to transport the body to the China Funeral Home and sent a telegram to his hometown, urging his family to come to Shanghai to claim the body.

A Truck Avoiding a Child Stopped Too Abruptly, Causing a Disaster—Worker Wei Chonghua Fell from the Truck and Died. 143

Wei Chonghua, a native of Xuzhou, 28 years old, worked as a porter in Peng Guiji's truck company at the Zhonghongqiao Pier. At around 8:00 AM yesterday, Wei and eight or nine other porters boarded Peng Guiji's truck, Concession Permit No. 16672, to go to Pudong to transport goods. As the truck passed the intersection of Pingliang Road and Qiwupu Road, it was speeding when suddenly a child appeared on the side of the road, seemingly wanting to cross the road. The driver, fearing an accident, braked suddenly. Unexpectedly, the force was too great, causing the porters standing on the truck to lose their balance and fall. Wei, who was standing on the edge, was thrown off the truck onto the ground. His head hit the brick and stone on the road, causing him to bleed profusely and lose consciousness. A nearby officer saw this and quickly helped him up and sent him to the hospital for treatment. However, due to the severity of his brain injury, he died in the afternoon. The body was transferred to the autopsy center.

Zheng Shiyue, a Woman, Sues Gu Chengda for Seduction and Abandonment; Verdict Scheduled for the 16th After Trial 149

Zheng Shiyue, a woman from Ningbo, is 20 years old and somewhat attractive. On the fourth day of the fourth lunar month of the 21st year of the Republic (1932), she married Gu Chengda, also from Ningbo. Later, due to financial difficulties, she became a saleswoman for the Great American Tobacco Company, earning 70-80 yuan per month, enough to make a living. At that time, due to her work, Zheng met Chen Mingxun, a 30-year-old man from Haiyan who owned the Rixin Chang foreign goods store at 29, 240 Lane, Edward Road, in September of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934). Chen was immediately attracted to Zheng’s graceful figure and charming appearance. He tried every means to seduce her, using his power and wealth to pressure her. Zheng,

tempted by the financial advantages, had a relationship with Chen at the Nanjing Hotel. Subsequently, Chen, fearing complications because Zheng was already married, incited her to break off her relationship with her husband. He claimed that he was unmarried and would marry Zheng if she divorced Gu Chengda. Zheng Shiyue, deceived by his words, believed him and discussed divorce with Gu Chengda. In the end, Gu Chengda was powerless to resist and had to reluctantly give in. On December 26th of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), both parties signed an agreement at lawyer Huang Xiuzhai's office, formally ending the marriage. Zheng gave Gu Chengda 360 yuan as

divorce compensation. Afterwards, Chen Mingxun immediately rented a house with Zheng at [omitted] Derun Lane, Luzon Road and began cohabitating. Soon after, they moved to No. 1, Lane 1370, Edward Road. At that time, Chen gave Zheng 300 yuan per month for living expenses, but he never mentioned marriage. Although Zheng urged him repeatedly, Chen Mingxun always evaded and made excuses. This spring, Chen suddenly changed his attitude, and it came to light that he had found new love and abandoned Zheng, even cutting off her living expenses. Zheng made several attempts to negotiate, but to no avail. She had no choice but to hire lawyer Wang Liangqing and file a

lawsuit of seduction and abandonment against Chen in the First Special Court's Criminal Division, requesting that Chen be punished according to Article 240, Section 2 and Article 239 of the Criminal Law, and to pay her living expenses of 300 yuan per month until she was 60 years old, totaling 144,000 yuan. The court approved the request and, on the 3rd of this month, entrusted Judge Huang Daxi to conduct the initial interrogation in the Fifth Criminal Court. Because the summons for Chen Mingxun could not be delivered at that time, only Zheng was interrogated, and the case was adjourned for a further hearing. Last Saturday was the date of the second hearing, Zheng

was absent due to illness. The defendant, Chen Mingxun, accompanied by his lawyer, arrived at the court on time. After a brief interrogation by the judge, Chen presented his defense in court, stating that the plaintiff, Zheng Shiyue, had worked as a prostitute in No. 82, Wufu Lane. In October of the 23rd year of the Republic (1934), the defendant was invited by a friend to visit and later invited friends to play mahjong twice, and they became acquainted. He had no intention of marrying the plaintiff or taking her as a family member, and he did not know whether she was married or encourage her to divorce. After obtaining the statements, the judge questioned them again, then instructed the lawyers of both parties to begin their arguments and declared the conclusion. The verdict will be announced on the afternoon of the 16th of this month.

Smuggled White Sugar Contains Large Amounts of Raw Gypsum; Can Harden into Stone in the Stomach; Hope People Do Not Seek Cheapness and Contract an Incurable Disease 150

According to the Shen Shi News Agency, smuggled white sugar has been imported in a steady stream recently, flooding the city and the interior, sold at low prices, and business is booming. The country's sugar producers have suffered from this invasion, and their inventories are piling up, putting them in a precarious situation. According to reporters' inquiries from the sugar industry, although the price of smuggled sugar is slightly cheaper than domestically produced sugar, its quality is very poor. The white sugar contains a large amount of finely ground raw gypsum. On the surface, it looks very white and weighs more, so people generally think it is cheap and good. But in reality, the sweetness is greatly reduced, and raw gypsum is very easy to settle in the stomach. Over time, it can harden into stone in the stomach. Therefore, it is hoped that people will not be greedy for smuggled sugar and risk contracting an incurable disease for a small price.

Young Woman Sentenced for Illicit Drug Trafficking 153

Police detectives Wang Ronggui and Zhu Jutong learned on June 17th that a young woman, Wei Sanjie, who lived at No. 92 Li Hai Road was secretly selling the drug morphine, in violation of the prohibition order. They rushed to the address and found 19 small packets of morphine and money worth 7 yuan and 2 jiao, and 12 double yuan in a wooden board under the stairs. They arrested Song Sanjie and Chen Songshi and took them to the police station, who said the husband was a user of opium, and did not dare to sell it. Chen Songshi stated that she had just arrived in Shanghai from her hometown and had borrowed 10 yuan from Song Sanjie. She was unaware of the drug trafficking. They were detained for further investigation. The case has been reported in this newspaper. The French Concession Police Department confirmed that the defendant was indeed engaged in illicit trafficking, filed a public prosecution in accordance with the Regulations on Prohibition of Opium and Narcotics. Judge Li Changnian held a final trial and sentenced Song Sanjie to one year in prison and one year of deprivation of civil rights. The confiscated morphine was ordered to be destroyed. Chen Songshi was found not guilty. After the judgment, Song Sanjie was sent to the detention center pending appeal, and Chen Songshi was allowed to provide a guarantor for release pending summons.

Lawyers Association Allocates 5,000 Yuan to Purchase Aircraft for Birthday Celebration 154

The Shanghai Lawyers Association decided at its spring general meeting to purchase an aircraft to celebrate Chairman Chiang Kai-shek's 50th birthday and notified all members of the donation method, which was divided into four levels: "Fortune, Prosperity, Longevity, Happiness." The first level, Fortune, was 100 yuan; the second level, Prosperity, was 50 yuan; the third level, Longevity, was 25 yuan; and the fourth level, Happiness, was 10 yuan. Although many members responded to the notification with donations, some were unable to contribute due to their limited financial resources. The association raised the matter for discussion at the recent joint meeting of the executive and supervisory committees and resolved to allocate 5,000 yuan of association funds for the purchase of an aircraft for the birthday celebration. The funds will be allocated and paid immediately. The Aviation Association's Purchase Aircraft for Birthday Celebration Committee has urged the association to remit the 5,000 yuan to the committee as soon as possible in preparation for the purchase of the aircraft for the birthday celebration.

Executive and Supervisory Committee Members of the Lawyers Association Visited the Second Prison Yesterday Morning 155

More than 30 members of the Executive and Supervisory Committee of the Shanghai Lawyers Association, including Shen Junru, Wang Manyun, and Mao Yun, gathered at the association's premises at No. 572, Belle Road in the French Concession at 8:00 AM yesterday (tomorrow is Sunday) and took a chartered car to visit the Jiangsu Second Prison in Caohejing at 8:30 AM. After arriving at the destination and presenting their cards, they were received by Warden Ding Lei and Section Chief Sun Peng of the prison and invited inside. After a short rest, they were accompanied to visit the prisoners' cells, workshops, and dining hall. At approximately 10:00 AM, they returned to Shanghai by the same car. The members, noting the recent hot weather and the large number of prisoners, were concerned about the possibility of disease and specially prepared a shipment of Ten Drops of Water, China Treasure Pill, and carbolic acid water to donate to the prison for use in case of illness.

Shi Ruisheng Arrested for Kidnapping a Young Woman 156

Xu Tiancai, a 68-year-old man from Yancheng, lives at No. 684, Jessfield Road, and has an 18-year-old daughter named Cuiying who is beautiful and charming. Recently, Shi Ruisheng, a neighbor from Wuxi, seduced her and had illicit relations with her. The day before yesterday, he hid Cuiying in the home of Wang Alin at No. [omitted], Hongkou. Cuiying's father discovered this and went to the location, where he apprehended Shi and Cuiying. They went together to Jessfield Road Police Station. After questioning them, the police station considered that the case involved the kidnapping of a young woman and prepared documents to send them to the General Bureau for interrogation.

Unsuccessful Extortion from a Prostitute, Slashed Silk Quilts in Revenge; Li Huicai Sentenced but Granted a Three-Year Reprieve 157

Li Huicai, a Cantonese man, together with several fellow Cantonese vagrants including Huang Guangyao, Yu Huachu, and Tan Guoliang (who were arrested and sentenced), went to the residence of Du Cuizhu, a prostitute at No. 1047, Gongyi Fang, North Sichuan Road, at 4:00 PM on the 4th of last month. They attempted to extort five yuan from her, but failed. They slashed two silk quilt covers with a knife and fled. At noon on the 6th of this month, Detective Chen Xikang and Fang Fucheng of the [omitted] Police discovered and arrested them on North Sichuan Road. A sharp knife was found on his person. He was taken to the First Special Court for questioning and denied the charges. He was ordered to be detained for a later hearing. Through the investigation of the Chinese and foreign detectives handling the case, it was discovered that Li and Huang Guangyao, who had been convicted, had gone to Gao Laowu, a prostitute at No. 6, Zenghui Li, Wuchang Road, on the 3rd of the same month, pawned two silk garments, a clock, and a pair of vases. Yesterday, Judge Xiao held a continued hearing. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, described the course of events and questioned the defendant. The defendant stated that Chen Cai invited him to go to Wuchang Road, and he was temporarily deceived and sought to evade the circumstances. The court sentenced Li Huicai to four months in prison, suspended for three years, and ordered the knife to be confiscated.

Middle School Student Bravely Pursues Robber 158

At approximately 2:00 AM yesterday, Hu Xiuying, a Cantonese woman residing at No. 12, Anshen Lane, Baoxing Road, Zhabei, was returning home when Liu Tongliu, a robber, suddenly snatched a handbag containing more than 20 yuan in silver currency. A Chinese middle school student, Feng Ruhao, witnessed the incident and gave chase, apprehending Liu and handing him over to the police at the North Station Sub-bureau for questioning. Due to the robbery charge, he was transferred to the Bureau for interrogation.

Young Woman Attempts Suicide with Poison 159

Jin Wu, a 23-year-old woman residing at No. 3, Xiderun Lane, Gonghe Road, Zhabei, had a dispute with her mother-in-law over a minor family matter at approximately 4:00 PM yesterday. She secretly swallowed four boxes of Red Head Self-Igniting Matches mixed with rice wine. Fortunately, her husband returned home and discovered her. She was immediately sent to Pushan Hospital for treatment. Doctor Jia Shirong managed to induce vomiting to expel the poison. Because the young woman was several months pregnant, her life is in grave danger.

Automobile Plunges into the Huangpu River 160

At 0:05 AM this morning, four passengers in a purple-red automobile went to the China Merchants Bureau's Jinliyuan Wharf on the Bund of the French Concession to board the Jianguo steamer. While the driver was reversing the car at the wharf in preparation for the return trip, the car unexpectedly plunged into the Huangpu River from the garbage wharf due to excessive speed. After witnessing the accident, they urgently reported it to the Songshan Road Police Station, which dispatched firefighters to rescue them. Because the car sank to the bottom of the river, it was impossible to salvage it. Therefore, the owner and model of the car are unknown. Yunfei and Yitai car companies confirm that all their vehicles are present and accounted for.

Four Tragic Deaths 161

Drowned: Xu Ruyou, a 17-year-old apprentice at the Zhenhua Dyeing Factory in Wuzhen Road, Zhabei, was from Shaoxing. He went to bathe in the river to escape the extreme heat on the evening of the day before yesterday. Unfortunately, the tide was high, and he was swept into the center of the river. His body was not found that night. At approximately 9:00 AM the next morning, the Water Patrol Division 2 discovered a floating corpse in the area. The local bailiff retrieved the body and brought it ashore. After identification by the court, Xu Rujin, the deceased's brother, arrived and identified the deceased as his brother Ruyou. He completed the formalities to retrieve the body for burial.

Drowned: Ni Buxiang, a 27-year-old local resident of No. 64, Yongxing Lane, Wuzhou Road, worked as a porter at Datong Wharf. Last night, he accidentally fell into the Huangpu River at the wharf and drowned. His body surfaced at approximately 11:00 AM the next morning at Wharf No. 15 of the River Patrol and was retrieved by police officer Fang Kui of the Water Patrol Team. The local bailiff requested the court to identify the body, and Li Xu of the deceased's family arrived to identify the body. They completed the formalities and retrieved the body for burial.

Drowned: Zhao Xiaohuaizi, a resident of Jiangbei who worked as a sailor at Nanmatou in the South City, accidentally fell into the water while cooling off on the bow of the ship late last night. At that time, the tide was rising, and the river was surging, so he drowned. His body was not found. The ship owner, Tang Heshang, reported the incident to the Water Patrol Headquarters and requested an investigation.

Suicide: At approximately 9:00 PM last night, people discovered the body of a woman hanging on a boat at No. [omitted], [omitted] Road, Zhabei. She had been dead for a long time. They reported the incident to the Water Patrol Division 2. Patrol Officer Xia Bin dispatched police officer Wang Chunlei to investigate. They first took down the body. They later determined that the deceased was named Qin Tang, 38 years old, from Yancheng. Her husband's name was Qin Lichang, and he worked as a rickshaw puller. The cause of her death is unknown. In addition to the bailiff guarding the scene, Zhang Zi, a prosecutor from the court, arrived to examine the body and confirmed that the deceased had died by hanging. They are awaiting the arrival of the family members to retrieve the body.

At approximately 5:00 PM yesterday, a fire broke out in a thatched shed at the intersection of Hongnan Mountain Road, Gonghe New Road, [omitted] and was quickly extinguished. Only one thatched shed was destroyed. However, an elderly man, Zhang Bucai, 60/66 years old, from Tongzhou, was burned during the fire. He was taken to Pushan Medical Center on Xinmin Road by a fire truck for treatment.

Yao Zhicheng Popularizes Smoking Cessation 163

Dr. Yao Zhicheng, a specialist in dermatology, graduated in medicine from Japan and established Zhicheng Hospital. The hospital is currently located at No. 3 Racecourse Road, opposite the Far East Hotel. He has been practicing medicine for 19 years and has treated tens of thousands of patients. Among Chinese Western medicine doctors in Shanghai, his injections and surgery have reached the highest level. Recently, Dr. Yao, motivated by the central government's strict prohibition of opium and narcotics, has made a grand vow to help society quit drug addiction. He spares no expense in compounding an extremely effective smoking cessation medication. Regardless of the length of addiction or the use of heroin, red pills, or other drugs, it can be safely discontinued. For the sake of helping the poor and needy, he charges very little and uses the fastest method. Hundreds of people have already quit smoking with Dr. Yao's help. Now he is striving to popularize it further. Those who are determined to quit addiction should pay attention.

Hongqiao Sanatorium in the [omitted] has seen a surge in consultations since establishing a comprehensive health examination department and a chest reshaping surgery department. The sanatorium is located in the western suburbs, an ideal location for recuperation in Shanghai. It can be reached in just six minutes by car from [omitted] Road, bottom Daxilu via the newly built Fales Road, or by taking a public bus to Zhaofeng Garden and transferring to a rickshaw via Fales Road, which is equally convenient.

Jiren Zhucai Association Ren Group Established 166

The Jiren Zhucai Association Ren Group has recruited 500 members, fulfilling the quota, and announced its establishment. Yesterday, they held a Buddhist service at the Great Hall of Qingliang Temple in Xin Family Garden, Xinzha Road, for two hours to pray for world peace. More than 400 members and 300 people from the Buddhist community attended. The meeting was called to order at 11:30 AM with the ringing of a bell. Shao Ruxin was elected as chairman. The ceremony was carried out as scheduled. First, the chairman reported on the purpose of the meeting and a summary of income and expenditure. He said, "Since I took over the reorganization and recruitment of members, it has been only three months in the midst of the sluggish business climate. Fortunately, the Ren Group has met its quota. So many comrades have attended today, which shows their enthusiasm for doing good deeds. I am very pleased. However, only 400 basic materials have been offered for donation, and only 20 or so have been recognized with assistance from important party and national figures like Mr. Chang Jingjiang and Mr. Weng Gang, a manager at Siemens. The difference is still significant, and the association has a funding shortfall. Please discuss this at length." The following key matters were discussed and resolved: 1. Each member will prepay one yuan for material production and one yuan for annual fees. 2. Actively preparing to establish the Jiren Chinese Medicine Hospital, scheduled to open on the first of next month. Medical assistance and drug dispensing expenses will be assumed by each member to the best of their ability. 3. After preparation, send a material assistance report form to each member (covering the return form) to begin material assistance. Thereafter, for each material worth 25 yuan, each member will only need to be responsible for 5 cents of material production costs. After assisting with 20 materials, members will be charged another yuan. 4. The chairman, Shao, will have full authority to appoint enthusiastic philanthropists to serve as directors. The association will never solicit a single penny from the outside world. All were approved. Subsequently, Grand Master Qinghai, President of the National Buddhist Association, arrived to bless all members. After the meeting, a photo was taken, and after lunch, the Buddhist community went to the main hall for two hours of Buddhist service to pray for peace. Chairman Shao led all members to the altar to burn incense and worship, creating a grand occasion.

Yellow Disaster Lottery Tickets Are Not Prohibited 167

Beijing News: There is news that the Executive Yuan has issued an order prohibiting the sale of Yellow River flood disaster lottery tickets. Now, according to Notice No. 4 of the Yellow River Flood Disaster Relief Lottery Office, "Recently, major newspapers in Tianjin, Shanghai, and Zhejiang have reported that the Executive Yuan has issued an order to stop the issuance of Yellow Disaster Lottery Tickets. The continued issuance of the Yellow River Flood Disaster Relief Lottery has been reported to the Executive Yuan by the Hebei-Chahar Political Affairs Committee for record. According to the reports, this is not the case. The fifteenth period will be drawn on schedule, and the sixteenth period will be issued as usual. In addition to having the relevant newspapers correct the reports, this notice is hereby issued." Since the publication of this notice in the city, the purchase of tickets has become even more enthusiastic.

The industrial use in our country, because there is no domestic product, has always relied on supplies from Germany and Japan, with annual outflows of no less than tens of thousands of pieces. The Zhong[omitted] Factory at Wangjiazhai, Kang[omitted] Road, Xiaodongmen, Shanghai, has always used the [omitted] brand of various lead oxides to resist imports and praised society [omitted]. Recently, in response to industrial needs, after careful research, it successfully developed a domestic lead acetate, which is pure in quality and no less than imported products. The price is lower [omitted], even cheaper than Japanese goods. The factory is willing to sacrifice profits to increase the credibility of domestic products and encourage trials in all fields. A large number of samples have been prepared and are offered completely free of charge. All factories in various regions are welcome to write to the distribution office of the Chinese Lead Red Factory at No. 2 Renyi Lane, Kangjia Street, Xiaodongmen, Shanghai, to request a sample, which will be sent immediately.

Sports News

Our National Football Team's European Tour - Written and Sent by Captain Li Huitang 174

Penang-Rangoon Voyage (June 20-23)

After drawing with the Penang team on June 19th, we set sail for Rangoon the next day in a light drizzle. The distance between the two places is approximately 800 nautical miles, requiring 65 hours of travel. This British Indian Steam Navigation Company passenger ship can be considered quite slow. This stretch of sea was the most uncomfortable among the many voyages since leaving the country. For three days, it was mostly wind and rain, with occasional thunder and lightning. The deep black sea waves, with their snow-white spray, were quite a spectacle. However, many members of our team were seasick. On the first day, most managed to hold on, forcing themselves to go to the dining room to eat, but later, unable to withstand it, six or seven out of ten spent most of their time on the small, soft berths. The next day, the number of participants in the morning exercises was less than a handful. Among them, Liang Rongzhao, Zhuo Shijin, Zheng Jiliang, and Ye Beihua were the most susceptible. To make matters worse, Xu Yahui even fell ill with chills and fever on the ship, speaking incoherently at times. Our injured players have not yet recovered, and now with the added concern of illness, I am truly worried about how we will cope with the upcoming matches.

Rangoon Diary (June 23-30)

(June 23) The weak and feeble sun, shining through the cabin window, woke us up early. Stretching out, we saw that the ship had already entered the Rangoon inland river. After three days of confinement, we were all delighted to see land again. Those who feared the waves were even more elated, as if they had been granted a pardon. Rangoon is the capital of British Burma, with flourishing commerce and can be considered one of the important cities in the South Seas region. Chinese merchants have a long history here, mostly from Fujian and Guangdong. The residents are very superstitious, hence Rangoon is known for "three things in abundance": temples, crows, and monks. The weather here is also said to be quite peculiar. It is extremely hot in March, April, and May, and the wealthy all flock to the mountains to escape the heat. Then come the rainy seasons in June, July, and August, with rain every day. No wonder we were greeted with misty rain after breakfast, shrouding the scenery of the fields on both sides of the river. At 8:30 AM, dozens of representatives from welcoming overseas Chinese organizations and the consulate had already arrived on a small boat to meet us. After checking our passports, the ship docked at the wharf. On the shore, crowds of overseas Chinese were eagerly waiting, and the band was playing loudly, braving the drizzle to greet us as we disembarked. Rangoon was a place we had never set foot in before, so everyone was particularly excited. What was most dissatisfying was the particularly strict customs inspection here, and we were not given any special treatment. We spent a good half an hour in the customs checkpoint. Afterwards, we lined up to exit the wharf and meet the overseas Chinese community. The applause was thunderous. It was the first time the Chinese team had visited, and the enthusiasm of the overseas Chinese was far greater than in other places. It is not surprising that a welcoming committee had been pre-arranged here, raising a large sum of money. The committee was responsible for all aspects of our team's food, lodging, and transportation, demonstrating their enthusiasm. After disembarking, we boarded several cars, led by a marching band, and toured the main streets of Rangoon. Whenever we passed through busy urban areas, Chinese and Westerners alike cheered to greet us, causing traffic jams and shaking the entire city. It was somewhat like the grand welcome that Lindbergh received upon returning to America after flying across the Atlantic. Along the way, we passed several Fujian and Guangdong temples, and at the suggestion of the leaders of the overseas Chinese community, the entire team entered to pay respects, praying for blessings during our stay here. Although this was somewhat superstitious, we did not want to offend the sincere intentions of the overseas Chinese, so we lined up and bowed three times. It is said that all "new arrivals" from the motherland must visit the temple upon arrival to avoid disaster. The depth of superstition is both pitiable and laughable. We circled the entire city and then returned to our team's lodging. The lodging was a new-style Western house, specially reserved for our team to stay in. Upstairs, there were dozens of beds, neatly arranged in rows, almost creating the impression of sleeping together under a large blanket. After lunch, because today was the King's birthday, the city held special horse races, and our team was invited to watch. The racetrack was about five miles from the city, with magnificent buildings, beautiful flowers and trees, and attractive pavilions. The racetracks in Hong Kong and Shanghai were not even comparable. We came with enthusiasm and all contributed money to gamble a little. Each time the horses were about to reach the finish line, everyone cheered and shouted for their chosen horse, acting like children, attracting the attention of the entire racetrack. Li Guowei was the luckiest, winning over eighty yuan on a long shot, and everyone rushed to congratulate him, urging him to treat us. In the evening, as we had been confined to the ship for three days, we declined all invitations and rested at our lodging.

Hsien Fang Cup Tennis - Youxing and Lingnan Both Win Big - Morning Light's Failure to Muster a Team is a Pity 175

The fifth Hsien Fang Cup Tennis League matches were held throughout the city yesterday. Chenguang had few players yesterday and could not form a team. Although they played the second singles and first doubles matches, according to Article 8 of the Cup Competition Rules, "At least four groups must participate in the competition, otherwise it will be considered a forfeit." The team could not complete a full match, so it was treated as a forfeit. Furthermore, if a team forfeits twice, its competition qualification will be revoked. It is hoped that Chenguang will pay special attention.

According to Mr. Lu, regarding the match between Lingnan and Lingxing reported yesterday, Zhao Ziqian of Lingxing said that many of their team members were participating in the Huacheng Cup and requested that Lingnan postpone the match, but the request was not granted, so it should be considered a forfeit. The statement that the match was not officially played is not accurate. In addition, Chen Bainian of Xiachun said that in the second doubles match against Meilu, his name was mistakenly reported as Wu Yangwu.

On the Conde Floating Platform En Route from Hong Kong to Singapore 180

— Special Correspondent Yi Qin

The ship was slow. Originally scheduled to arrive in Hong Kong at 2:00 PM on the 28th, it was delayed until 4:45 PM, stopping at the Kowloon commercial port on the opposite shore. The Hong Kong Chinese Amateur Athletic Federation had already dispatched a special small boat to welcome all the delegation members, ferrying them to the Hong Kong port. Those who came to welcome us included Mr. Xie Yuchuan, Mr. Yan Chengkun (who had returned from Singapore to Hong Kong a few days ago), and Mr. Lu Xiafu, among others, totaling over a dozen people. After the small boat arrived at the Star Ferry pier, we boarded specially prepared public buses to attend the welcoming reception hosted by the Chinese Amateur Athletic Federation. During the reception, Chairman Xie delivered a welcoming speech, followed by speeches of thanks from Mr. Shen Siliang and Superintendent Hao Gengsheng, who expressed their gratitude. After the meeting, the delegation members went to the commercial center to purchase miscellaneous items. When returning to the ship, everyone was carrying packages and Hong Kong newspapers. Delegation member Xiao was quite concerned about national affairs. We returned to the floating platform at 7:00 PM, and set sail directly for Singapore around 8:00 PM.

Those who boarded the ship in Hong Kong included the nine members of the observation delegation: Xu Minhui, Liu Beida, Ye Guantao, Tan Bin, Guo Songtang, and athletes Huang Jiliang (football), Yang Xiuqiong, Chen Zhenxing (swimming), and Huang Yingjie (track and field). After leaving Hong Kong, various organizations within the delegation were gradually established. The Administrative Committee was composed of Shen Siliang, Hao Gengsheng, Yuan Dunli, John Ma, Lao Te, Gao Zi, Zhou Jiaqi, and Shi Qikang. There was also a Lecture Committee composed of Yuan Dunli, Gao Zi, and Wu Cheng. The first lecture was given by Hao Gengsheng on the morning of the 29th, titled "The Current Situation of Chinese Education." In addition to the delegation members, many passengers also attended. Other activities were also very active. The Training Committee stipulated that starting from June 30th, morning exercises would be held on the deck every day from 7:00 AM to 7:30 AM (except Sundays), and all delegation members were required to attend, led in rotation by the following individuals:

(June 30th) John Ma (July 1st) Huang Liming (2nd) Hao Ming (3rd) Wu Cheng (4th) Wang Huaiqi (6th) Dong Shouyi (7th) Song Junfu (8th) Ye Liang (9th) Gao Zi (10th) Hou Luoxun (11th) Shao Rugan (13th) Qian Yiqin (14th) Li Zhou (15th) Wang Shoufang (16th) Li Youzhen (17th) Wu Bangwei (18th) Park Longyuan. There was also a German conversation class, with 28 delegation members participating, divided into four groups (A, B, C, D), taught by Courtful, Wu Cheng, and Huang Yuankai. The Entertainment Committee held a Chinese chess championship from July 1st to 4th, with 18 delegation members participating. Among them, Wu Demao, Lin Shaozhou, Feng Youzhen, and Qian Yiqin were considered the most likely to win. The first entertainment gathering was scheduled to be held at 9:00 PM on the evening of July 2nd, and the program mostly consisted of national martial arts performances, Peking opera, and Cantonese opera, promising a lively atmosphere. On the evening of July 1st, all delegation members practiced singing together, and will continue to practice in preparation for use in the Olympic Games. In addition to reading, writing letters, and playing chess, many of the athletes were also practicing sports and swimming. There were two small pools on the ship, less than 20 feet long and no more than 10 feet wide, so there was quite a crowd. The ship also had movie facilities, which were viewed by different classes of passengers. Since the start of the voyage, two movies have been shown, and many delegation members watched them. Around 10:00 AM on the morning of July 2nd, we arrived in Singapore. No fewer than two hundred people came to welcome us at the pier, each holding a national flag and shouting the slogan "Victory to the Chinese Delegation!" After disembarking, we departed from Tanjong Pagar Wharf and toured the city by public bus. After the tour, we went to the grand welcoming reception jointly organized by the overseas Chinese organizations at the Great World amusement park. The delegation also held a basketball exhibition game at 4:00 PM in the afternoon, and were scheduled to return to the ship at 5:30 PM on the same day to set sail for Colombo.

Hua Cheng Cup Tennis Second Week - Carson Easily Defeats Chen Yi Yesterday 181

The first Kangdi Open Tennis Hua Cheng Cup singles tournament, yesterday was the second week, with sixteen groups competing. The games started at 9:00 AM and finished around 6:00 PM, held in three sessions. The most intense matches yesterday were Zhao Junzhao vs. Dong Junpei, Li Guofan vs. Ye Baosheng, Shi Guia vs. Feng Yipei, and Shen Meizhen vs. Zhou Guanjun. However, Carson's victory over Chen Yi was particularly hard-won. In the first set, Chen won two games in a row, but Carson gradually caught up. Then Chen again surpassed Carson with a score of 3-2, but Carson won three consecutive games, taking the lead at 5-3. Chen did not lose heart and managed to tie the score. At this point, Carson's baseline shots were ineffective, so he quickly moved to the net for volleys and finally won the first set 7-5. In the second set, after Chen won the first game, Carson took five games in a row. Although Chen fought hard, he was unable to reverse the situation and lost to Carson 6-2. Carson is the most promising candidate for this year's championship, and Chen Yi was indeed no match for him. Kerasha's victory over Xu Demin was entirely due to Xu's poor serving. The competition between Shi Guia and Feng Yipei was fierce. In the final match, Shen Meizhen vs. Zhou Guanjun, Zhou led 6-2 in the first set. It was drizzling, but the two continued to play. Shen pulled back with 6-3 in the second set. The last set was crucial. Shen became excited and played barefoot, but her strength was insufficient and she lost again with 6-1. Education News

Education Construction Funds for the 25th Year Have Been Allocated; Funding for Compulsory Education Increased Compared to Last Year 187

The National Government has also allocated 5 million yuan for the fourth item, education construction funds, within the seventh item, education and culture expenses, of the temporary expenditure section of the budget for the 25th year of the Republic of China. It is stated that this 5 million yuan is for expenses such as compulsory education, mass education, film broadcasting education, etc. It is reported that the central education authorities have recently held meetings and finalized the allocation of compulsory education funds to various provinces and cities. The Ministry of Education will soon issue telegrams to inform the provinces and cities. The allocation method for mass education, film broadcasting education, and other expenses will be decided in meetings to be held within days. It is noted that in the 24th year, the central government subsidized 2.4 million yuan for compulsory education expenses to various provinces and cities, plus tens of thousands of yuan from the Sino-British and other Gengkuan institutions, totaling 3.2 million yuan. In the current 25th year, all provinces and cities are making great efforts to promote compulsory education, and the actual need for funds is very large. On one hand, provinces, cities, and localities are raising funds themselves, and on the other hand, they are still requesting special subsidies from the central government. The central government has also taken this into consideration, so in the 25th year, 5 million yuan has been allocated for education construction expenses. In addition to paying about one million yuan for mass education, film broadcasting education, and other expenses, the compulsory education item, including Gengkuan subsidies, will total approximately 4.4 million yuan, an increase of about 1.2 million yuan compared to the 24th year.

Shanghai Branch of the Cultural Construction Association Organizes an Invention Exhibition - Enthusiastic Participation - Deadline for Submissions is August 10th - Opening in Shanghai on October 1st 188

The Shanghai Branch of the Chinese Cultural Construction Association is organizing an invention exhibition to promote new inventions and encourage future generations. The organizing committee has been actively preparing for the exhibition. Since the collection of exhibits began on June 1st, there has been enthusiastic participation from various regions. The deadline for registration is set for August 10th, and the public exhibition will open on October 1st. The exhibition welcomes submissions of (1) new inventions, (2) new discoveries, (3) improvements in product quality or manufacturing methods in the past ten years that have proven successful, (4) the first imitation of foreign products that have been approved by government agencies, and (5) inventions or new discoveries from before the past ten years that have made significant contributions to culture. Submissions of humanistic, agricultural, industrial, and artistic categories are welcome.

Student Dietary Nutrition - Survey by the Chinese Society of Natural Sciences 192

The Chinese Society of Natural Sciences is conducting a survey of the nutritional composition of the diets of students and their families in various regions to compile statistics for reference. Forms have been prepared and distributed to health education committees in various regions for distribution to schools to be filled out. The survey content includes (1) the name, weight, or volume of the food consumed today, (2) the actual number of diners and their ages, (3) the number of meals eaten by guests today, (4) the number of family members who did not eat at home, (5) the amount of food left over today, (6) any diseases suffered by people in the household, and (7) the most common diseases suffered by adults and children.

Zhang's National Studies Lecture Hall - Adds a Preparatory Class 195

Zhang Taiyan established the Zhang's National Studies Lecture Hall in Suzhou. After Zhang's death, Chairman Chiang donated 3,000 yuan as a condolence gift. Now, his wife, Ms. Tang Guoli, will use the funds as the start-up cost for a preparatory class in the lecture hall, and she will serve as the director. This year, 40 new students will be admitted. The following is a simplified outline: 1. One-year term: Students will complete one year of study and then be promoted to the lecture hall to attend lectures. 2. Curriculum: Classics, Model Essays, Academic Essays, Composition, Philology, Ma's Grammar, Comprehensive Mirror for Aid in Government, Selected Readings from the Masters, Selected Poems, Calligraphy, and National Arts. 3. Fees: Tuition is free. Full board is 35 yuan per semester, half board is 17 yuan, lodging is 5 yuan, miscellaneous fees are 5 yuan, and lecture notes are 3 yuan. Dormitories are not currently available for female students. 4. Requirements: High school graduation or equivalent. 5. Admission: A composition test will be held on the morning of August 15th, and a general knowledge of national studies oral examination will be held in the afternoon. 6. Registration: Registration at the Association in Jinfan Road, Suzhou. Registration fee is one yuan. Please submit a 2.5-inch half-length photo and graduation certificate.

Ministry of Education Orders the Issuance of Standards for School Hygiene Facilities (2) 196

(II) Correction of Deficiencies: All deficiencies discovered during physical examinations, marked with (20) symbols, should be corrected. Deficiencies marked with (30) symbols should be corrected immediately. Trachoma, dental, skin, and ear diseases should be corrected in each school. For deficiencies such as tonsils, vision, nose, heart, lungs, and hernia, efforts should be made to have them properly corrected at local hospitals. (III) Follow-up Examinations of Deficiencies: All cases of trachoma, skin diseases, ear diseases, and other eye diseases should be re-examined once before the end of each semester. Dental deficiencies should be re-examined once a year. Other deficiencies should be re-examined periodically as appropriate. (IV) Periodic Measurements: Height and weight should be measured once at the beginning and end of each semester. Weight should be measured once a month at a fixed time. Class teachers or nurses are responsible for the measurements. (V) Morning Inspections: Class teachers should conduct morning inspections every morning. During the inspection, attention should be paid to the children's cleanliness, neatness, and other hygiene habits, as well as symptoms of various acute infectious diseases. If symptoms of suspected acute infectious diseases are found, the child should be immediately stopped from attending school and sent to a doctor or nurse for re-examination. 3. Prevention of Infectious Diseases: (I) Vaccination: Vaccination should be administered uniformly at the same time as physical examinations. Depending on local conditions, typhoid and cholera vaccinations should be administered annually or every other year. Diphtheria vaccination may be administered to the extent possible. (II) Infectious Disease Management: If a class teacher discovers symptoms of suspected infectious diseases in a child, the child should be immediately sent to a doctor or nurse for examination. If the diagnosis is confirmed as an infectious disease, the patient should be immediately isolated, and those in contact with the patient should be subjected to appropriate quarantine. At the same time, the local health education authority should be notified to implement necessary disinfection procedures. 4. Environmental Hygiene: (I) The window area of the classroom should account for one-fifth of the floor area. (II) The classroom should be equipped with air vents, but fresh, cold air should not be allowed to strike the children's heads directly. (III) The desks and chairs in the classroom should be suitable for the children's height. The chair height should allow the children to place both feet flat on the floor when sitting, with the knees forming a right angle of "ninety-seven degrees." The desk height should allow the distance between the tabletop and the students' eyes to be about 35 centimeters when sitting upright. (IV) The wall where the blackboard is hung should not have windows, and the blackboard should not be reflective. (V) The arrangement of children's seats should allow light to enter from the left. (VI) A drinking water tank should be placed outside each classroom, and each student should have a teacup for drinking. (VII) The floor and doors and windows of the classroom should be washed with water at least once a week. (VIII) The school should have clean toilets with screen windows and doors. Feces in the pits should be removed once a day. The number of toilet pits should be as follows:

Number of Female Toilet Pits: (4) (30-50 students) (5) (50-70) (6) (70-150) (8) (150-200) (10) (4) (200-300) (10) (8) (300-400)

Number of Male Toilet Pits: (2) (30-50 students) (3) (50-70) (4) (70-150) (5) (150-200) (7) (200-300) (8) (300-400)

If the school does not have a dormitory, the number of pits can be reduced by one-third. (IX) Handwashing facilities should be available near the toilets. (X) The dining hall should have screen windows and doors, and the bowls and chopsticks should be boiled and washed with boiling water. Improvement of the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University - Renamed to Five Departments Including Horticulture 197

The Agricultural College of Zhejiang University originally had three departments: Agricultural Botany, Zoology, and Rural Sociology, with each department divided into several groups. It is now reported that the dean of the college, Wu Fuzhen, has decided to reorganize the college starting this year. It has been decided to rename the departments to five: Horticulture, Agronomy, Sericulture, Plant Pathology and Entomology, and Agricultural Economics. The original animal husbandry and forestry groups have been abolished, and students will transfer to the Agricultural College of Central University to study. It is said that there will also be changes in the faculty of the college in the second half of the year.
